  1. Q: What is the difference between Freestyle and Pipeline jobs?
    A: Freestyle is UI-configured with no version control; Pipeline uses a Jenkinsfile in Git with stages, parameters, and parallel execution. Pipeline is preferred for maintainable test automation.
  2. Q: How do you trigger a Jenkins job on Git push?
    A: Configure a webhook in Git (GitHub/GitLab) pointing to Jenkins, enable "GitHub hook trigger" in the job, or use SCM polling as fallback.
  3. Q: What is a Multibranch Pipeline and why use it for QA?
    A: It auto-creates jobs per branch/PR. QA uses it to run smoke on feature branches and full regression on develop/release without manual job creation.
  4. Q: How do you run a specific TestNG suite in a Freestyle job?
    A: Maven build step: mvn test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml. Post-build: publish JUnit results from target/surefire-reports/*.xml.
  5. Q: What are limitations of Freestyle jobs for automation teams?
    A: Not version-controlled, no parallel stages, hard to parameterize, difficult to replicate across environments, no PR branch auto-discovery.
  6. Q: When would you choose Scripted over Declarative Pipeline?
    A: When you need dynamic stage generation (e.g., loop over 10 environments), complex Groovy logic, or non-standard flow that Declarative syntax cannot express.
  7. Q: How do you organize multiple test jobs in Jenkins?
    A: Use Folders (Smoke, Regression, Nightly) or a single Pipeline with parameters for suite selection. Multibranch for branch-based execution.
  8. Q: What post-build actions are essential for test jobs?
    A: Publish JUnit/TestNG results, archive HTML reports and failure screenshots, email notification on failure, optionally mark unstable vs failed.

Real Project Example

An e-commerce automation team started with 3 Freestyle jobs (smoke, regression, nightly). Maintenance became painful when they added 4 environments and 3 browsers. They migrated to a Multibranch Pipeline: PRs triggered smoke (10 tests, 3 min), merges to develop ran API + UI regression (150 tests, 25 min), and nightly cron ran full cross-browser suite. Jenkinsfile lived in the automation repo; QA reviewed pipeline changes alongside test code.

Common Mistakes

  • Hardcoding credentials in Freestyle job config instead of Jenkins Credentials
  • Using SCM polling (every minute) instead of webhooks—wastes resources and delays feedback
  • Not publishing test results—team only sees "BUILD FAILURE" without knowing which tests failed
  • Creating separate Freestyle jobs per browser instead of parameterized Pipeline
  • Forgetting to archive screenshots/logs on failure—impossible to debug CI-only failures

Troubleshooting Tips

  • Job not triggering on push: Verify webhook delivery in GitHub → Settings → Webhooks; check Jenkins URL is reachable from Git server.
  • Git checkout fails: Verify credentials ID in job matches Jenkins Credentials; check branch name pattern.
  • Maven not found: Configure Maven in Global Tool Configuration; reference in Pipeline with tools { maven 'Maven-3.9' }.
  • Tests pass locally but fail in Jenkins: Check env vars, headless browser config, and different JDK/Maven versions.
  • Multibranch not discovering branches: Run "Scan Multibranch Pipeline Now"; verify Jenkinsfile exists on branch root.

Quick Revision Notes

  • Freestyle = UI config, no version control, good for POC
  • Pipeline = Jenkinsfile in Git, parameterized, parallel, reusable
  • Multibranch = auto branch/PR jobs, ideal for PR smoke validation
  • Triggers: webhook (best) > SCM polling > cron (nightly)
  • Always publish JUnit results + archive reports/screenshots

Section 9: Jenkins Pipelines — Deep Dive

Pipelines are how automation engineers define test execution as code. Your Jenkinsfile is as important as your Page Object Model—it's the orchestration layer for every test run in CI/CD.

Pipeline as Code

Store the Jenkinsfile in your project root (same repo as tests). Jenkins checks out the repo and executes the Jenkinsfile. Changes to pipeline logic go through the same PR review process as test code.

Convention: Place Jenkinsfile at repo root. For Multibranch, Jenkins auto-detects it. For standalone Pipeline job, specify "Pipeline script from SCM."

Declarative Pipeline — Full Example

pipeline {
    agent any
    tools { maven 'Maven-3.9' }
    parameters {
        choice(name: 'BROWSER', choices: ['chrome', 'firefox', 'edge'], description: 'Browser')
        choice(name: 'ENV', choices: ['qa', 'staging', 'prod'], description: 'Environment')
        choice(name: 'SUITE', choices: ['smoke', 'regression', 'full'], description: 'Test Suite')
    }
    stages {
        stage('Checkout') {
            steps { git branch: 'main', url: 'https://github.com/team/automation.git' }
        }
        stage('Build') {
            steps { bat 'mvn clean compile' }
        }
        stage('Execute Tests') {
            steps {
                bat "mvn test -Dbrowser=${params.BROWSER} -Denv=${params.ENV} -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=${params.SUITE}.xml"
            }
        }
        stage('Generate Reports') {
            steps {
                publishHTML([
                    allowMissing: false,
                    alwaysLinkToLastBuild: true,
                    keepAll: true,
                    reportDir: 'target/surefire-reports',
                    reportFiles: 'index.html',
                    reportName: 'Test Report'
                ])
            }
        }
    }
    post {
        always {
            archiveArtifacts artifacts: 'target/**', allowEmptyArchive: true
        }
        success {
            emailext subject: 'Build Passed',
                     body: 'All tests passed for ${params.SUITE} on ${params.ENV}.',
                     to: 'team@company.com'
        }
        failure {
            emailext subject: 'Build Failed',
                     body: 'Tests failed. Check Jenkins: ${BUILD_URL}',
                     to: 'team@company.com'
        }
    }
}

Keyword Reference — Declarative Pipeline

KeywordPurposeAutomation Example
pipelineRoot block; declares Declarative PipelineWraps entire test job definition
agentWhere pipeline runs (any, label, docker, none)agent any runs on any available Jenkins agent
toolsAuto-install/config tools from Global Tool Configurationmaven 'Maven-3.9', nodejs 'Node-18'
parametersUser inputs at build timeBrowser, environment, suite selection dropdowns
stagesContainer for all pipeline stagesGroups Checkout, Build, Test, Report stages
stageSingle logical phase with a namestage('Execute Tests')
stepsActual commands inside a stagebat 'mvn test', sh 'npm test'
postActions after all stages completeArchive artifacts, send emails regardless of outcome
alwaysRuns every time (pass, fail, abort)Archive test reports even on failure
successRuns only when all stages passSend "all green" email to team
failureRuns when any stage failsSend failure alert with build URL

Scripted Pipeline

node {
    stage('Checkout') { checkout scm }
    stage('Build')     { sh 'mvn clean compile' }
    stage('Test')      { sh 'mvn test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml' }
}

Scripted Pipeline uses imperative Groovy. Use it when:

  • Dynamic stage generation (loop over environments or test modules)
  • Complex conditional logic that Declarative when cannot express
  • Shared libraries with advanced Groovy functions
  • Legacy pipelines migrated from Scripted before Declarative existed
Recommendation: Start with Declarative. Only switch to Scripted when you hit a genuine limitation. Most test automation pipelines never need Scripted.

Pipeline Syntax Elements

agent

agent any                              // any available node
agent { label 'windows-selenium' }     // specific agent with browsers installed
agent { docker { image 'maven:3.9-eclipse-temurin-17' } }  // containerized
agent none                             // no global agent; set per stage

environment

environment {
    TEST_ENV = 'qa'
    BASE_URL = 'https://qa.example.com'
    BROWSER  = "${params.BROWSER}"
}

when — Conditional Stage Execution

stage('Regression') {
    when {
        expression { params.SUITE == 'regression' }
    }
    steps { bat 'mvn test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=regression.xml' }
}

stage('Prod Tests') {
    when { branch 'release/*' }
    steps { bat 'mvn test -Denv=prod' }
}

parallel — Simultaneous Stages

stage('Cross-Browser') {
    parallel {
        stage('Chrome') {
            steps { bat 'mvn test -Dbrowser=chrome -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml' }
        }
        stage('Firefox') {
            steps { bat 'mvn test -Dbrowser=firefox -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml' }
        }
    }
}

input — Manual Approval Gate

stage('Deploy to Staging') {
    steps {
        input message: 'Smoke passed. Deploy to staging and run regression?', ok: 'Deploy'
        bat 'mvn test -Denv=staging -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=regression.xml'
    }
}

timeout — Stage Timeout

stage('Regression') {
    options { timeout(time: 60, unit: 'MINUTES') }
    steps { bat 'mvn test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=regression.xml' }
}

retry — Retry Failed Stage

stage('Smoke') {
    options { retry(2) }
    steps { bat 'mvn test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml' }
}

Complete Automation Pipeline Example

Checkout → Build → Smoke (parallel Chrome+Firefox) → Regression → Report → Email → Deploy

pipeline {
    agent any
    tools { maven 'Maven-3.9' }
    parameters {
        choice(name: 'ENV', choices: ['qa', 'staging'], description: 'Target Environment')
        booleanParam(name: 'RUN_REGRESSION', defaultValue: true, description: 'Run full regression?')
    }
    environment {
        BASE_URL = "${params.ENV == 'qa' ? 'https://qa.example.com' : 'https://staging.example.com'}"
    }
    stages {
        stage('Checkout') {
            steps { checkout scm }
        }
        stage('Build') {
            steps { bat 'mvn clean compile -DskipTests' }
        }
        stage('Smoke Tests') {
            parallel {
                stage('Smoke - Chrome') {
                    steps {
                        bat 'mvn test -Dbrowser=chrome -Dheadless=true -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml'
                    }
                }
                stage('Smoke - Firefox') {
                    steps {
                        bat 'mvn test -Dbrowser=firefox -Dheadless=true -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml'
                    }
                }
            }
        }
        stage('Regression') {
            when { expression { params.RUN_REGRESSION } }
            options { timeout(time: 90, unit: 'MINUTES') }
            steps {
                bat "mvn test -Denv=${params.ENV} -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=regression.xml"
            }
        }
        stage('Generate Reports') {
            steps {
                junit 'target/surefire-reports/*.xml'
                publishHTML([
                    reportDir: 'target/surefire-reports',
                    reportFiles: 'emailable-report.html',
                    reportName: 'TestNG Report',
                    keepAll: true
                ])
            }
        }
        stage('Deploy to QA') {
            when { branch 'develop' }
            steps {
                input message: 'Tests passed. Proceed with QA deployment?', ok: 'Deploy'
                bat 'echo Deploying build to QA environment...'
            }
        }
    }
    post {
        always {
            archiveArtifacts artifacts: 'target/surefire-reports/**, screenshots/**',
                               allowEmptyArchive: true
        }
        success {
            emailext subject: "PASS: ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER}",
                     body: "All stages passed.\nBuild: ${env.BUILD_URL}",
                     to: 'qa-automation@company.com'
        }
        failure {
            emailext subject: "FAIL: ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER}",
                     body: "Pipeline failed. Check: ${env.BUILD_URL}",
                     to: 'qa-automation@company.com',
                     attachLog: true
        }
    }
}

Pipeline Best Practices (10 Points)

  1. Keep Jenkinsfile in Git — never edit pipeline in Jenkins UI (Cheat option breaks version control).
  2. Use parameters for browser, environment, suite — avoid hardcoding values.
  3. Always publish test results — junit 'target/surefire-reports/*.xml' in a dedicated Report stage or post { always }.
  4. Archive artifacts on failure — screenshots, logs, HTML reports for debugging CI-only failures.
  5. Set stage timeouts — prevent hung browser sessions from blocking agents for hours.
  6. Use parallel for independent suites — cross-browser smoke, API + UI simultaneously.
  7. Separate smoke from regression — fast feedback on PR; heavy suite on merge/nightly.
  8. Use credentials binding — withCredentials for passwords/tokens, never plain text in Jenkinsfile.
  9. Add retry for flaky smoke — options { retry(1) } on smoke stage only, not regression.
  10. Keep stages focused — one responsibility per stage; easier to identify failure point in Blue Ocean/graph.

Interview Questions

  1. Q: What is Pipeline as Code?
    A: Defining CI/CD pipeline in a Jenkinsfile stored in Git. Benefits: version control, code review, reproducibility across Jenkins instances.
  2. Q: Explain Declarative vs Scripted Pipeline.
    A: Declarative uses structured syntax (pipeline { stages { } }) with built-in validation and post conditions. Scripted uses free Groovy in node { } for maximum flexibility.
  3. Q: What does agent any mean?
    A: Run the pipeline on any available Jenkins agent/node. Use agent { label 'windows' } when tests need a specific OS or installed browsers.
  4. Q: How do you run Chrome and Firefox tests in parallel?
    A: Use parallel { stage('Chrome'){...} stage('Firefox'){...} } inside a parent stage. Each parallel branch needs its own workspace or isolated execution.
  5. Q: What is the post block?
    A: Runs after all stages complete. Conditions: always, success, failure, unstable, changed. Used for archiving, notifications, cleanup.
  6. Q: How do you add a manual approval before regression?
    A: Use input message: 'Approve regression run?', ok: 'Proceed' as a step before the regression stage.
  7. Q: What is when directive?
    A: Conditionally executes a stage based on branch, parameter value, environment, or custom expression. E.g., run regression only when params.SUITE == 'regression'.
  8. Q: How do you pass Maven properties from Jenkins parameters?
    A: Interpolate in shell step: bat "mvn test -Dbrowser=${params.BROWSER}". Parameters are available via params.PARAM_NAME.
  9. Q: What happens if a stage times out?
    A: Jenkins aborts the stage and marks the build as failed. Configure with options { timeout(time: 30, unit: 'MINUTES') }.
  10. Q: How do you skip a stage based on a boolean parameter?
    A: when { expression { params.RUN_REGRESSION } } on the stage block.
  11. Q: Difference between bat and sh?
    A: bat for Windows agents (cmd.exe); sh for Linux/Mac agents (bash). Match your Jenkins agent OS.
  12. Q: How do you publish TestNG HTML report in Pipeline?
    A: Use HTML Publisher Plugin: publishHTML([reportDir: '...', reportFiles: 'index.html', reportName: '...']) plus junit for trend graphs.

Real Project Example

A banking QA team replaced 6 Freestyle jobs with one Declarative Pipeline. Parameters: ENV (dev/qa/staging), BROWSER, SUITE (smoke/regression). PR builds ran smoke in parallel on Chrome+Firefox (4 min). Merge to develop triggered regression (45 min) with 90-min timeout. Post block archived ExtentReports and emailed team with pass/fail counts. Pipeline changes required PR approval—eliminating "someone changed the Jenkins job and broke nightly" incidents.

Common Mistakes

  • Editing pipeline via "Replay" or UI instead of committing Jenkinsfile changes to Git
  • Not setting timeouts— hung WebDriver sessions block agents indefinitely
  • Running regression on every PR (slow feedback); should be smoke only on PR
  • Using sh on Windows agents or bat on Linux agents
  • Hardcoding URLs/credentials instead of parameters and credentials binding
  • Parallel stages writing to same workspace without isolation—causes test interference

Troubleshooting Tips

  • Pipeline syntax error: Use Declarative Pipeline Linter (Workflow CPS plugin) or "Pipeline Syntax" generator in job config.
  • Parameter not recognized: Run job once after adding parameters (Jenkins needs initial build to register them).
  • Parallel stage fails randomly: Ensure ThreadLocal WebDriver and separate test data per thread.
  • post block not running: Check for uncaught exception before stages complete; use post { always }.
  • Maven command works in console but not pipeline: Add tools { maven '...' } or use full path to mvn.

Quick Revision Notes

  • Declarative = structured, validated, preferred for test pipelines
  • Key blocks: pipeline → agent → parameters → stages → post
  • parallel = cross-browser; when = conditional; input = approval gate
  • timeout + retry = control flaky/hung test runs
  • Always: junit + archiveArtifacts + email in post block

Section 10: Jenkins + TestNG Integration

TestNG is the most common test framework integrated with Jenkins in Java/Selenium automation projects. This section covers Maven execution, suite XML design, pipeline integration, parallel runs, and failure handling—from an automation engineer's workflow perspective.

TestNG Execution via Maven

Run TestNG suites through Maven Surefire plugin:

mvn test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=src/test/resources/testng/smoke.xml
mvn test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml -Dbrowser=chrome -Denv=qa

Surefire Plugin Configuration in pom.xml

<build>
  <plugins>
    <plugin>
      <groupId>org.apache.maven.plugins</groupId>
      <artifactId>maven-surefire-plugin</artifactId>
      <version>3.2.5</version>
      <configuration>
        <suiteXmlFiles>
          <suiteXmlFile>${suiteXmlFile}</suiteXmlFile>
        </suiteXmlFiles>
        <systemPropertyVariables>
          <browser>${browser}</browser>
          <env>${env}</env>
        </systemPropertyVariables>
        <testFailureIgnore>false</testFailureIgnore>
      </configuration>
    </plugin>
  </plugins>
</build>
Pass suite at runtime: -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml overrides pom.xml default. Pass browser/env as Maven properties consumed by your framework's config reader.

TestNG XML Files for Different Suites

Suite FilePurposeTestsDurationWhen to Run
smoke.xmlCritical path validation~10 tests~2 minEvery PR, post-commit
regression.xmlFull functional coverage~200 tests~45 minNightly, pre-release
sanity.xmlModule-specific checks~30 tests~10 minPost-deployment, hotfix validation
crossbrowser.xmlChrome + Firefox parallel~50 tests × 2 browsers~15 minWeekly, release candidate

Example: smoke.xml

<!DOCTYPE suite SYSTEM "https://testng.org/testng-1.0.dtd">
<suite name="Smoke Suite" parallel="false">
  <test name="Login and Checkout">
    <classes>
      <class name="com.app.tests.LoginTest"/>
      <class name="com.app.tests.CheckoutTest"/>
    </classes>
  </test>
</suite>

Example: crossbrowser.xml (parallel methods)

<suite name="Cross Browser" parallel="methods" thread-count="4">
  <parameter name="browser" value="chrome"/>
  <test name="UI Tests">
    <classes>
      <class name="com.app.tests.SearchTest"/>
      <class name="com.app.tests.CartTest"/>
    </classes>
  </test>
</suite>

Jenkins Pipeline for TestNG

pipeline {
    agent any
    tools { maven 'Maven-3.9' }
    parameters {
        choice(name: 'SUITE', choices: ['smoke', 'regression', 'sanity', 'crossbrowser'],
               description: 'TestNG Suite')
        choice(name: 'BROWSER', choices: ['chrome', 'firefox', 'edge'], description: 'Browser')
        choice(name: 'ENV', choices: ['qa', 'staging'], description: 'Environment')
    }
    stages {
        stage('Checkout') {
            steps { checkout scm }
        }
        stage('Run TestNG') {
            steps {
                bat """
                    mvn clean test \
                      -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=src/test/resources/testng/${params.SUITE}.xml \
                      -Dbrowser=${params.BROWSER} \
                      -Denv=${params.ENV}
                """
            }
        }
        stage('Publish Results') {
            steps {
                junit testResults: 'target/surefire-reports/*.xml', allowEmptyResults: false
                publishHTML([
                    reportDir: 'target/surefire-reports',
                    reportFiles: 'emailable-report.html',
                    reportName: 'TestNG HTML Report',
                    keepAll: true,
                    alwaysLinkToLastBuild: true
                ])
            }
        }
    }
    post {
        failure {
            archiveArtifacts artifacts: 'screenshots/**, target/surefire-reports/**',
                               allowEmptyArchive: true
            emailext subject: "TestNG FAILED: ${params.SUITE} on ${params.ENV}",
                     body: "Build ${env.BUILD_URL}\nCheck surefire reports for failed tests.",
                     to: 'qa-team@company.com'
        }
        always {
            archiveArtifacts artifacts: 'target/surefire-reports/*.xml', allowEmptyArchive: true
        }
    }
}

TestNG Results Plugin

  • JUnit plugin (junit step) reads TestNG XML output from target/surefire-reports/
  • Displays pass/fail/skip counts on build page
  • Trend graph: "Test Result Trend" shows test count and failures over last N builds
  • Click failed test name to see stack trace without opening console log

Parallel Execution Setup

testng.xml Configuration

<suite name="Parallel Suite" parallel="methods" thread-count="5">
  <test name="Parallel Tests">
    <classes>
      <class name="com.app.tests.AccountTests"/>
    </classes>
  </test>
</suite>

Requirements

  • Jenkins agent executors: Set # executors ≥ thread-count on the agent label
  • ThreadLocal WebDriver: Each thread must have its own driver instance—never share static WebDriver across parallel tests
  • Independent test data: Use unique user accounts or data factories per thread to avoid collisions
  • Grid for heavy parallel: Local machine may handle 5 threads; 20+ threads need Selenium Grid

TestNG + Jenkins Workflow

Git Push → Webhook → Jenkins Job Triggered ↓ Checkout automation repo ↓ mvn test (Surefire → TestNG) ↓ target/surefire-reports/*.xml generated ↓ Jenkins JUnit Plugin parses results ↓ Trend graph updated + Email sent ↓ (Pass) Merge allowed / (Fail) Block PR

Handling TestNG Failures in Pipeline

Failed Build vs Unstable Build

SettingBuild StatusUse Case
testFailureIgnore=false (default)FAILURESmoke on PR—must block merge
testFailureIgnore=trueSUCCESS (tests still reported)Informational nightly run (not recommended for gates)
Cucumber/TestNG plugin buildStatus: 'UNSTABLE'UNSTABLENon-blocking regression; team notified but deploy continues

Post-Action on Failure

post {
    failure {
        junit 'target/surefire-reports/*.xml'
        archiveArtifacts artifacts: 'screenshots/**, logs/**'
        emailext subject: 'Test Failures Detected',
                 body: '${FAILED_TESTS, showStackTrace=true}',
                 to: 'qa-team@company.com'
    }
}
Automation Engineer Note: Prefer fixing flaky tests over setting testFailureIgnore=true. Unstable builds erode trust in CI signal.

Interview Questions

  1. Q: How do you run a specific TestNG XML suite via Maven?
    A: mvn test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml. Configure Surefire plugin in pom.xml to accept the property.
  2. Q: Where does TestNG write results for Jenkins?
    A: target/surefire-reports/TEST-*.xml. Jenkins JUnit plugin parses these files.
  3. Q: How do you parameterize browser and environment from Jenkins?
    A: Pass as Maven system properties: -Dbrowser=${params.BROWSER} -Denv=${params.ENV}. Framework reads via System.getProperty().
  4. Q: What is parallel="methods" in TestNG?
    A: Runs @Test methods concurrently across threads. Requires ThreadLocal WebDriver and thread-safe test data.
  5. Q: Difference between failed and unstable build for tests?
    A: FAILURE blocks pipeline/deploy; UNSTABLE indicates test failures but allows pipeline to continue (use for non-gating suites).
  6. Q: How do you show TestNG trend graph in Jenkins?
    A: Publish JUnit results consistently every build. Jenkins auto-generates "Test Result Trend" on job page.
  7. Q: What happens if surefire reports directory is empty?
    A: Build may fail at junit step. Use allowEmptyResults: true only when tests might legitimately not run.
  8. Q: How to run different suites on different branches?
    A: Multibranch Pipeline with when { branch 'feature/*' } for smoke and when { branch 'develop' } for regression.
  9. Q: Can you run multiple suite XML files in one Maven command?
    A: Yes: -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml,api.xml or define multiple suites in pom.xml.
  10. Q: How do you archive TestNG emailable report?
    A: HTML Publisher Plugin pointing to target/surefire-reports/emailable-report.html plus archiveArtifacts in post block.

Real Project Example

A SaaS company ran 180 TestNG tests across 4 suite files. PR pipeline: smoke.xml (12 tests, 3 min). Nightly: regression.xml (180 tests, 40 min) with parallel="methods" thread-count=5. Jenkins published JUnit trends—when failures spiked after a release, QA caught a regression within hours. Failure emails included ${FAILED_TESTS} token listing exact test names and stack traces.

Common Mistakes

  • Static shared WebDriver with parallel="methods"—causes random failures and session conflicts
  • Wrong path to suite XML—use repo-relative path matching pom.xml structure
  • Not publishing JUnit results—team cannot see which @Test methods failed
  • Running full regression on every commit—kills developer feedback loop
  • Setting testFailureIgnore=true to "make pipeline green"—hides real failures

Troubleshooting Tips

  • 0 tests run: Check suite XML class names match package; verify Surefire includes **/*Test.java.
  • Tests pass locally, fail in Jenkins: Compare JDK version, env properties, headless mode, test data availability.
  • Parallel tests flaky only in CI: Reduce thread-count; verify ThreadLocal driver; check for shared test accounts.
  • No trend graph: Ensure junit step runs every build with same report path pattern.
  • Maven property not reaching TestNG: Define in surefire systemPropertyVariables or pass via -D flag.

Quick Revision Notes

  • Execute: mvn test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=<suite>.xml
  • Suites: smoke (PR), regression (nightly), sanity (post-deploy), crossbrowser (weekly)
  • Jenkins: junit step + publishHTML + archiveArtifacts on failure
  • Parallel: thread-count in XML + ThreadLocal WebDriver + enough executors
  • Failure handling: FAILURE blocks merge; UNSTABLE for non-gating runs

Section 11: Jenkins + Cucumber Integration

Cucumber BDD tests integrate with Jenkins through Maven, tag-based filtering, and dedicated reporting plugins. As an automation engineer, you control which scenarios run on PR vs nightly through tags and pipeline parameters.

Cucumber Execution via Maven

mvn test -Dcucumber.filter.tags="@smoke"
mvn test -Dcucumber.filter.tags="@regression and not @wip"
mvn test -Dcucumber.filter.tags="@sanity and @api"

Runner Class

@CucumberOptions(
    features = "src/test/resources/features",
    glue = "com.app.stepdefinitions",
    tags = "@smoke",
    plugin = {"pretty", "html:target/cucumber-report.html",
              "json:target/cucumber-report.json"}
)
public class TestRunner extends AbstractTestNGCucumberTests { }
Cucumber 7+: Use cucumber.filter.tags Maven property to override runner tags at runtime without changing code.

Tag-Based Execution Strategy

TagTriggerDurationPipeline Behavior
@smokePR validation~5 minBlocks merge on failure
@regressionNightly cron~1 hrEmail on failure; non-blocking for deploy
@sanityPost-deployment~10 minValidates critical flows after release
@apiAPI-only suite~15 minFast backend validation without UI
@wipExcluded alwaysN/Anot @wip in every CI run

Jenkins Pipeline for Cucumber

pipeline {
    agent any
    tools { maven 'Maven-3.9' }
    parameters {
        choice(name: 'TAGS',
               choices: ['@smoke', '@regression', '@sanity', '@api'],
               description: 'Cucumber Tags')
        choice(name: 'ENV', choices: ['qa', 'staging'], description: 'Environment')
    }
    stages {
        stage('Checkout') {
            steps { checkout scm }
        }
        stage('Test') {
            steps {
                bat "mvn clean test -Dcucumber.filter.tags=\"${params.TAGS}\" -Denv=${params.ENV}"
            }
        }
        stage('Report') {
            steps {
                cucumber buildStatus: 'UNSTABLE',
                         jsonReportDirectory: 'target',
                         fileIncludePattern: '**/*.json'
                publishHTML([
                    reportDir: 'target',
                    reportFiles: 'cucumber-report.html',
                    reportName: 'Cucumber HTML Report',
                    keepAll: true
                ])
            }
        }
    }
    post {
        failure {
            archiveArtifacts artifacts: 'target/cucumber-report.json, screenshots/**'
            emailext subject: "Cucumber ${params.TAGS} FAILED",
                     body: "Check report at ${env.BUILD_URL}",
                     to: 'qa-team@company.com'
        }
    }
}

Cucumber Reports Plugin

  • Reads JSON reports from target/**/*.json
  • Displays feature/scenario breakdown with pass/fail/skip/undefined
  • Click scenario to see step-level results and error messages
  • buildStatus: 'UNSTABLE' — marks build unstable (not failed) when scenarios fail
  • buildStatus: 'FAILURE' — use for @smoke PR gates that must block merge

Parallel Cucumber Execution

Use TestNG DataProvider with parallel execution in the runner:

@DataProvider(parallel = true)
@Override
public Object[][] scenarios() {
    return super.scenarios();
}

Combined with TestNG suite XML:

<suite name="Cucumber Parallel" parallel="methods" thread-count="4">
  <test name="Cucumber Tests">
    <classes>
      <class name="com.app.runners.ParallelTestRunner"/>
    </classes>
  </test>
</suite>
Each parallel scenario needs isolated WebDriver (ThreadLocal) and independent test data. Feature files tagged @serial should run in a separate non-parallel job.

Cucumber + Allure Integration in Jenkins

pom.xml — Allure Cucumber Plugin

<plugin>
  <groupId>io.qameta.allure</groupId>
  <artifactId>allure-maven</artifactId>
  <version>2.12.0</version>
</plugin>

Pipeline — Generate and Publish Allure

stage('Allure Report') {
    steps {
        bat 'mvn allure:report'
        allure includeProperties: false,
               jdk: '',
               results: [[path: 'target/allure-results']]
    }
}

Allure shows scenario steps, attachments (screenshots on failure), and trend history across builds.

Interview Questions

  1. Q: How do you run Cucumber scenarios by tag in Jenkins?
    A: Pass Maven property: -Dcucumber.filter.tags="@smoke". Jenkins parameter lets QA select tag at build time.
  2. Q: What is AbstractTestNGCucumberTests?
    A: Base class that integrates Cucumber with TestNG, enabling TestNG features (parallel, listeners, reporting) with Cucumber scenarios.
  3. Q: How does Cucumber Reports Plugin work?
    A: Parses JSON output from Cucumber runs, displays feature/scenario results in Jenkins UI, can set build status to UNSTABLE or FAILURE.
  4. Q: How to exclude WIP scenarios from CI?
    A: Use tag expression: @regression and not @wip in Maven command or runner config.
  5. Q: Difference between @smoke and @sanity tags?
    A: @smoke = minimal critical paths for fast PR feedback. @sanity = broader post-deployment validation of key modules after release.
  6. Q: How to run @smoke on PR and @regression nightly in one repo?
    A: Multibranch Pipeline with different tag parameters, or two pipeline jobs with different cron/webhook triggers and TAGS parameter defaults.
  7. Q: How do you parallelize Cucumber scenarios?
    A: Override scenarios() DataProvider with parallel=true in runner extending AbstractTestNGCucumberTests; set thread-count in testng.xml.
  8. Q: What JSON path does Cucumber Reports Plugin expect?
    A: Configure jsonReportDirectory and fileIncludePattern: '**/*.json'—typically target/cucumber-report.json.
  9. Q: When to use buildStatus UNSTABLE vs FAILURE?
    A: FAILURE for merge-blocking smoke; UNSTABLE for informational nightly regression where deploy should continue.
  10. Q: How to integrate Allure with Cucumber in Jenkins?
    A: Add allure-cucumber7-jvm dependency, configure allure-maven plugin, use allure step in pipeline pointing to target/allure-results.

Real Project Example

An insurance portal had 320 Cucumber scenarios across 45 feature files. Tags: @smoke (18 scenarios), @regression (all), @api (backend only). PR webhook triggered Jenkins Multibranch with @smoke and not @wip (4 min). Nightly cron ran @regression and not @wip with parallel DataProvider (thread-count=4, 55 min). Cucumber Reports Plugin showed failing scenario steps; product owners reviewed Allure reports linked from Jenkins email.

Common Mistakes

  • Forgetting not @wip—half-written scenarios fail CI
  • Not generating JSON report—Cucumber Reports Plugin has nothing to parse
  • Same tag on too many scenarios—@smoke suite grows to 30 min, defeating PR fast feedback
  • Parallel scenarios sharing browser session—use ThreadLocal WebDriver
  • Hardcoding tags in runner instead of Maven property—requires code change to switch suites

Troubleshooting Tips

  • 0 scenarios run: Verify tag spelling matches feature files; check tag expression syntax (and/or/not).
  • Undefined steps in CI only: Glue path mismatch; ensure all step definition packages are on classpath.
  • Cucumber plugin shows no data: Confirm JSON file exists in configured directory after test stage.
  • Parallel failures: Reduce thread-count; isolate @serial tagged features into separate job.
  • Allure empty: Verify allure-cucumber dependency version matches Cucumber 7.x.

Quick Revision Notes

  • Run by tag: mvn test -Dcucumber.filter.tags="@smoke"
  • Runner extends AbstractTestNGCucumberTests for TestNG integration
  • PR=@smoke, Nightly=@regression, Post-deploy=@sanity, Backend=@api
  • Cucumber Reports Plugin reads JSON; set buildStatus appropriately
  • Parallel via DataProvider(parallel=true) + ThreadLocal driver

Section 12: Jenkins + Selenium

Running Selenium in Jenkins requires understanding local vs headless vs Grid execution, browser driver management, and artifact collection on failure. This section focuses on what automation engineers configure—not server administration.

Local Execution

Jenkins agent runs on the same machine where ChromeDriver/GeckoDriver are installed. Suitable for small teams or dedicated automation VMs with browsers pre-installed.

  • Install browsers and matching driver versions on the Jenkins agent
  • Set driver path via system property or WebDriverManager in framework
  • Limitation: single machine resources; cannot scale parallel browsers easily

Headless Execution

CI servers typically have no display (GUI). Headless mode runs browsers without a visible window.

Why Headless in CI

  • No GUI/display server required on Linux CI agents
  • Faster execution—no rendering overhead
  • Standard approach for Jenkins, GitHub Actions, Azure DevOps agents

Configuration Code

ChromeOptions options = new ChromeOptions();
if (Boolean.parseBoolean(System.getProperty("headless", "true"))) {
    options.addArguments("--headless=new");
    options.addArguments("--window-size=1920,1080");
    options.addArguments("--disable-gpu");
    options.addArguments("--no-sandbox");
    options.addArguments("--disable-dev-shm-usage");
}
WebDriver driver = new ChromeDriver(options);
Pass from Jenkins: mvn test -Dheadless=true -Dbrowser=chrome. Always set window-size in headless—default 800×600 causes element visibility failures.

Remote Execution with Selenium Grid

Hub-Node Architecture

  • Hub: Central router receiving test requests (port 4444)
  • Nodes: Worker machines/containers with browsers; hub assigns sessions
  • Tests use RemoteWebDriver pointing to hub URL
DesiredCapabilities caps = new DesiredCapabilities();
caps.setBrowserName("chrome");
WebDriver driver = new RemoteWebDriver(
    new URL("http://selenium-grid:4444/wd/hub"), caps);

Docker Grid — docker-compose.yml

version: "3.8"
services:
  selenium-hub:
    image: selenium/hub:4.21.0
    container_name: selenium-hub
    ports:
      - "4444:4444"
    environment:
      - SE_NODE_MAX_SESSIONS=4

  chrome-node:
    image: selenium/node-chrome:4.21.0
    depends_on:
      - selenium-hub
    environment:
      - SE_EVENT_BUS_HOST=selenium-hub
      - SE_EVENT_BUS_PUBLISH_PORT=4442
      - SE_EVENT_BUS_SUBSCRIBE_PORT=4443
      - SE_NODE_MAX_SESSIONS=4
    shm_size: 2gb

  firefox-node:
    image: selenium/node-firefox:4.21.0
    depends_on:
      - selenium-hub
    environment:
      - SE_EVENT_BUS_HOST=selenium-hub
      - SE_EVENT_BUS_PUBLISH_PORT=4442
      - SE_EVENT_BUS_SUBSCRIBE_PORT=4443
      - SE_NODE_MAX_SESSIONS=4
    shm_size: 2gb

Start Grid before tests: docker-compose up -d. Jenkins pipeline passes -Dgrid.url=http://localhost:4444/wd/hub.

Complete Selenium Pipeline

pipeline {
    agent any
    tools { maven 'Maven-3.9' }
    parameters {
        choice(name: 'BROWSER', choices: ['chrome', 'firefox', 'edge'])
        booleanParam(name: 'HEADLESS', defaultValue: true, description: 'Headless mode')
        string(name: 'GRID_URL', defaultValue: 'http://localhost:4444/wd/hub',
               description: 'Selenium Grid URL (empty for local)')
    }
    stages {
        stage('Checkout') {
            steps { checkout scm }
        }
        stage('Build') {
            steps { bat 'mvn clean compile -DskipTests' }
        }
        stage('Selenium Tests') {
            steps {
                bat """
                    mvn test \
                      -Dbrowser=${params.BROWSER} \
                      -Dheadless=${params.HEADLESS} \
                      -Dgrid.url=${params.GRID_URL} \
                      -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml
                """
            }
        }
        stage('Report') {
            steps {
                junit 'target/surefire-reports/*.xml'
                publishHTML([
                    reportDir: 'target/surefire-reports',
                    reportFiles: 'index.html',
                    reportName: 'Selenium Test Report',
                    keepAll: true
                ])
            }
        }
    }
    post {
        failure {
            archiveArtifacts artifacts: 'screenshots/**, target/surefire-reports/**',
                               allowEmptyArchive: true
            emailext subject: "Selenium Tests FAILED - ${params.BROWSER}",
                     body: "Screenshots archived. ${env.BUILD_URL}",
                     to: 'qa-team@company.com'
        }
        always {
            junit allowEmptyResults: true, testResults: 'target/surefire-reports/*.xml'
        }
    }
}

Screenshot Archiving on Failure

@AfterMethod
public void captureScreenshot(ITestResult result) {
    if (result.getStatus() == ITestResult.FAILURE) {
        File src = ((TakesScreenshot) driver.get())
                     .getScreenshotAs(OutputType.FILE);
        Files.copy(src.toPath(),
            Paths.get("screenshots/" + result.getName() + ".png"),
            StandardCopyOption.REPLACE_EXISTING);
    }
}

Jenkins post { failure { archiveArtifacts 'screenshots/**' } } makes screenshots downloadable from build page.

Selenium Grid 4 with Docker in Jenkins

  1. Install Docker on Jenkins agent (or use dedicated Grid server)
  2. Add stage to start Grid: sh 'docker-compose -f docker/grid-compose.yml up -d'
  3. Wait for hub ready: sh 'curl --retry 10 --retry-delay 5 http://localhost:4444/status'
  4. Run tests pointing to Grid URL
  5. Post always: sh 'docker-compose down' to free resources

Interview Questions

  1. Q: Why run Selenium headless in Jenkins?
    A: CI agents lack display/GUI. Headless runs Chrome/Firefox without a visible window, faster and no Xvfb needed (with --headless=new).
  2. Q: What ChromeOptions are essential for CI?
    A: --headless=new, --window-size=1920,1080, --no-sandbox, --disable-dev-shm-usage (Docker).
  3. Q: Explain Selenium Grid hub-node architecture.
    A: Hub routes test requests; nodes execute browsers. Enables parallel cross-browser execution across machines/containers.
  4. Q: How do tests connect to Grid from Jenkins?
    A: RemoteWebDriver with hub URL passed as Maven property: -Dgrid.url=http://grid:4444/wd/hub.
  5. Q: Why is shm_size: 2gb needed in Docker Grid?
    A: Default /dev/shm (64MB) is too small for Chrome; causes crashes. Increase shared memory in docker-compose.
  6. Q: How to archive failure screenshots in Jenkins?
    A: Test listener saves to screenshots/ on @AfterMethod failure; pipeline archiveArtifacts 'screenshots/**' in post failure block.
  7. Q: Local vs Grid execution—when to use each?
    A: Local for dev/single-browser smoke. Grid when parallel sessions exceed agent capacity or cross-browser scaling needed.
  8. Q: Tests pass headless locally but fail in Jenkins—common causes?
    A: Different screen resolution, missing --no-sandbox in Docker, driver/browser version mismatch, timing issues (need explicit waits).
  9. Q: How to run Chrome and Firefox in parallel on Grid?
    A: Jenkins parallel stages each invoking mvn test with different -Dbrowser value, both pointing to same Grid hub.
  10. Q: What is WebDriverManager role in CI?
    A: Auto-downloads matching driver for installed browser version—reduces "driver version mismatch" failures on agents.

Real Project Example

A fintech team ran 80 Selenium tests on Jenkins Windows agent initially (sequential, 50 min). Migrated to Docker Grid 4 on a Linux VM: 4 Chrome + 2 Firefox nodes. Pipeline started Grid, ran smoke in parallel stages (Chrome + Firefox, 8 min total), archived screenshots on 3 failing tests—QA downloaded PNGs directly from Jenkins without reproducing locally. Headless + Grid cut nightly regression from 50 min to 18 min.

Common Mistakes

  • Missing --window-size in headless—elements reported as not visible/interactable
  • Not increasing Docker shm_size—Chrome crashes with "session deleted" errors
  • Forgetting to tear down Grid containers—memory exhaustion on agent over time
  • Hardcoding Grid URL instead of Jenkins parameter—breaks when Grid moves
  • Not archiving screenshots—CI-only failures impossible to debug

Troubleshooting Tips

  • Session not created: Browser/driver version mismatch—use WebDriverManager or Selenium 4 built-in driver management.
  • Timeout connecting to Grid: Verify hub is up (/status endpoint); check firewall between Jenkins agent and Grid.
  • Chrome crashed in Docker: Add --no-sandbox, increase shm_size, ensure enough RAM for node containers.
  • Tests slower in CI: Normal—add explicit waits; avoid Thread.sleep; consider Grid scaling.
  • Screenshots empty/black: Headless screenshot timing—take screenshot after page load complete.

Quick Revision Notes

  • CI = headless + window-size + no-sandbox (Docker)
  • Grid = hub routes, nodes execute; scale parallel browsers
  • Pipeline params: BROWSER, HEADLESS, GRID_URL
  • Always archive screenshots/** on failure
  • Docker Grid: shm_size 2gb, tear down in post always

Section 13: Jenkins + Playwright

Playwright is increasingly chosen for CI/CD due to built-in auto-waiting, native parallelism, and multi-browser support. Automation engineers using TypeScript/JavaScript/Python can integrate Playwright into Jenkins with Node.js tooling.

Why Playwright in CI/CD

  • Fast: Auto-wait eliminates most flaky timing issues
  • Reliable: Built-in retry, trace viewer for debugging CI failures
  • Built-in parallelism: --workers=N without Grid setup
  • Multi-browser: Chromium, Firefox, WebKit from single test code
  • Headless by default in CI—no extra configuration needed

Playwright Setup in Jenkins

  1. Install NodeJS Plugin in Jenkins → Global Tool Configuration → add Node.js 18+
  2. Pipeline references: tools { nodejs 'Node-18' }
  3. Install dependencies: npm ci (uses package-lock.json—reproducible)
  4. Install browsers: npx playwright install --with-deps
  5. Run tests: npx playwright test

Jenkins Pipeline for Playwright

pipeline {
    agent any
    tools { nodejs 'Node-18' }
    parameters {
        choice(name: 'PROJECT', choices: ['chromium', 'firefox', 'webkit', 'all'],
               description: 'Browser project')
        string(name: 'WORKERS', defaultValue: '4', description: 'Parallel workers')
    }
    stages {
        stage('Install') {
            steps {
                bat 'npm ci'
                bat 'npx playwright install --with-deps'
            }
        }
        stage('Test') {
            steps {
                script {
                    if (params.PROJECT == 'all') {
                        bat "npx playwright test --workers=${params.WORKERS} --reporter=html,list"
                    } else {
                        bat "npx playwright test --project=${params.PROJECT} --workers=${params.WORKERS} --reporter=html,list"
                    }
                }
            }
        }
        stage('Report') {
            steps {
                publishHTML([
                    reportDir: 'playwright-report',
                    reportFiles: 'index.html',
                    reportName: 'Playwright HTML Report',
                    keepAll: true,
                    alwaysLinkToLastBuild: true
                ])
            }
        }
    }
    post {
        failure {
            archiveArtifacts artifacts: 'playwright-report/**, test-results/**',
                               allowEmptyArchive: true
            bat 'npx playwright show-report --host 0.0.0.0 || echo Report archived'
        }
        always {
            junit allowEmptyResults: true,
                  testResults: 'test-results/junit.xml'
        }
    }
}
Add JUnit reporter in playwright.config.ts: reporter: [['html'], ['junit', { outputFile: 'test-results/junit.xml' }]] for Jenkins trend graphs.

Parallel and Cross-Browser Execution

# Parallel workers (same browser)
npx playwright test --workers=4

# Cross-browser via projects in playwright.config.ts
npx playwright test --project=chromium --project=firefox --project=webkit

# Run specific tag
npx playwright test --grep @smoke

playwright.config.ts — Multi-Project

export default defineConfig({
  workers: process.env.CI ? 4 : 2,
  retries: process.env.CI ? 1 : 0,
  reporter: [['html'], ['junit', { outputFile: 'test-results/junit.xml' }]],
  projects: [
    { name: 'chromium', use: { ...devices['Desktop Chrome'] } },
    { name: 'firefox',  use: { ...devices['Desktop Firefox'] } },
    { name: 'webkit',   use: { ...devices['Desktop Safari'] } },
  ],
});

Playwright vs Selenium in CI/CD

AspectPlaywrightSelenium
Setup in JenkinsNode.js + npm ci + playwright installJava/Maven + browser drivers or Grid
Parallel ExecutionBuilt-in workers, no Grid neededRequires Grid or TestNG parallel + ThreadLocal
HeadlessDefault in CIManual ChromeOptions configuration
FlakinessAuto-wait reduces timing issuesRequires explicit waits; more flaky in CI
Debugging CI FailuresTrace viewer, screenshot/video on failureManual screenshot listener setup
Cross-BrowserChromium, Firefox, WebKit nativeChrome, Firefox, Edge (WebKit limited)
Report in JenkinsHTML report + JUnit XMLTestNG/Extent + JUnit XML
Best ForModern JS/TS automation teamsJava teams with existing Selenium frameworks

Report Publishing

  • HTML Reporter: Default playwright-report/index.html — publish via HTML Publisher Plugin
  • JUnit XML: Enables Jenkins test trend graphs
  • Allure: @playwright/test + allure-playwright reporter for rich CI reports
  • Traces: Enable trace: 'on-first-retry' — archive test-results/ for offline trace analysis

Containerized Playwright Execution

stage('Test in Container') {
    agent {
        docker {
            image 'mcr.microsoft.com/playwright:v1.44.0-jammy'
            args '-u root:root'
        }
    }
    steps {
        sh 'npm ci'
        sh 'npx playwright test --workers=4'
    }
}

Microsoft's Playwright Docker image includes browsers and dependencies—no separate playwright install needed. Ideal for consistent CI environments.

Interview Questions

  1. Q: How do you set up Playwright in Jenkins?
    A: NodeJS plugin → tools { nodejs } → npm ci → npx playwright install --with-deps → npx playwright test.
  2. Q: Why use npm ci instead of npm install in CI?
    A: npm ci installs exact versions from package-lock.json—reproducible builds; faster and stricter than npm install.
  3. Q: How to run Playwright tests in parallel?
    A: --workers=4 or set workers in playwright.config.ts. Playwright manages browser contexts internally.
  4. Q: How to publish Playwright report in Jenkins?
    A: HTML Publisher Plugin on playwright-report/index.html; add JUnit reporter for trend graphs.
  5. Q: Playwright vs Selenium for CI/CD?
    A: Playwright has built-in parallelism, auto-wait, trace debugging—less infrastructure (no Grid). Selenium suits existing Java/TestNG investments.
  6. Q: What is mcr.microsoft.com/playwright Docker image?
    A: Official image with browsers and OS deps pre-installed—consistent CI without manual browser setup on agents.
  7. Q: How to debug Playwright CI failures?
    A: Enable trace/video/screenshot on failure; archive test-results/ folder; use Playwright trace viewer locally.
  8. Q: How to run cross-browser in one Jenkins build?
    A: Define projects in config; run npx playwright test --project=chromium --project=firefox --project=webkit.

Real Project Example

A startup migrated 60 UI tests from Selenium+Grid to Playwright. Jenkins pipeline: Node-18 agent, npm ci, playwright install, test with --workers=4 (8 min vs previous 25 min on Grid). HTML report published per build; on failure, archived traces let developers replay exact CI steps locally in trace viewer—reduced "cannot reproduce" tickets by 70%.

Common Mistakes

  • Using npm install instead of npm ci—non-reproducible dependency versions
  • Skipping playwright install --with-deps on fresh agents—browser binary not found
  • Not configuring JUnit reporter—no test trend in Jenkins
  • Running all browser projects sequentially without parallel projects config
  • Not archiving test-results/ on failure—lose traces and screenshots

Troubleshooting Tips

  • Browser not found: Run npx playwright install --with-deps or use official Docker image.
  • Tests pass locally, fail in Jenkins: Check baseURL env var, CI retries setting, viewport size differences.
  • HTML report empty: Ensure --reporter=html and report generated before publishHTML step.
  • Out of memory with workers=8: Reduce workers or use agent with more RAM; each worker launches browser context.
  • Permission denied on Linux agent: Use Playwright Docker image or install system deps via --with-deps.

Quick Revision Notes

  • Setup: NodeJS plugin → npm ci → playwright install → playwright test
  • Parallel: --workers=N; cross-browser: --project flags
  • Reports: HTML (publishHTML) + JUnit XML (trend graph)
  • Docker: mcr.microsoft.com/playwright for consistent CI
  • Debug: trace on failure, archive test-results/

Section 14: Test Execution Strategy in CI/CD

Test execution strategy defines what runs, when, and what happens on failure. As an automation engineer, you design suite tiers and pipeline gates—not just write tests. This section covers categorization, suite design, promotion, quality gates, flaky management, and test data.

Test Categorization for CI/CD

CategoryTestsDurationTriggerFail ActionPriority
PR Validation (Smoke)~20 critical path~5 minEvery PR / pushBlock mergeP0
Post-MergeSmoke + API (~70)~15 minMerge to developNotify team; flag buildP1
Nightly RegressionFull suite (~500)1–2 hrsCron 2 AMEmail; create defect ticketsP1
Weekly Cross-BrowserUI × 3 browsers2–3 hrsWeekly SundayReport to QA leadP2
Release / UATSanity + UAT scenarios~30 minRelease branch cutBlock releaseP0
PerformanceLoad/stress subset~1 hrWeekly / pre-releaseReview with devopsP2
Golden Rule: PR feedback under 10 minutes. If smoke exceeds that, split into slimmer smoke + move checks to post-merge tier.

Test Suite Design for Pipelines

Suite FileScopeTest CountPipeline Stage
smoke.xmlLogin, checkout, payment—critical paths only~20PR validation
api.xmlREST/GraphQL endpoints, no UI~50Post-merge, parallel with smoke
regression.xmlAll functional tests~500Nightly cron
crossbrowser.xmlUI tests × Chrome, Firefox, Edge~50 × 3Weekly, release candidate
sanity.xmlPost-deploy health checks~30After QA/staging deploy

Build Promotion Strategy

Developer Push / PR │ ▼ ┌─────────────┐ Fail ──→ Block Merge │ Smoke Tests │ │ └──────┬──────┘ │ │ Pass │ ▼ │ ┌─────────────┐ │ │ Merge to │ │ │ develop │ │ └──────┬──────┘ │ ▼ │ ┌─────────────┐ Fail ──→ Notify Team │ Deploy QA │ │ └──────┬──────┘ │ ▼ │ ┌─────────────┐ Fail ──→ Hold Promotion │ Regression │ │ │ (QA) │ │ └──────┬──────┘ │ │ Pass │ ▼ │ ┌─────────────┐ │ │Deploy Staging│ │ └──────┬──────┘ │ ▼ │ ┌─────────────┐ Fail ──→ Block Release │ UAT/Sanity │ │ └──────┬──────┘ │ │ Pass │ ▼ │ ┌─────────────┐ │ │ Production │◄───────────────────┘ │ Deploy │ (fix & re-run) └─────────────┘

Quality Gates

Quality gates are automated pass/fail criteria before promotion to the next environment.

GateThresholdEnforced AtImplementation
Pass Rate> 95%Nightly, releaseJenkins checks JUnit results count; fail if below threshold
No P1/P2 Failures0 critical failuresReleaseTag tests @P1/@P2; pipeline fails if any tagged test fails
All Smoke Pass100% smoke passPR, every deployHard gate—no testFailureIgnore
Code Coverage> 80%PR (optional)JaCoCo report; SonarQube quality gate
No New Flaky TestsFlaky rate < 2%Weekly reviewTrack retry-pass tests in dashboard
 
stage('Quality Gate') {
    steps {
        script {
            def testResults = junit testResults: 'target/surefire-reports/*.xml'
            def passRate = (testResults.passCount / testResults.totalCount) * 100
            if (passRate < 95) {
                error("Pass rate ${passRate}% below 95% threshold")
            }
        }
    }
}

Flaky Test Management

RetryAnalyzer in TestNG

public class RetryAnalyzer implements IRetryAnalyzer {
    private int count = 0;
    private static final int MAX_RETRY = 2;

    @Override
    public boolean retry(ITestResult result) {
        if (count < MAX_RETRY) { count++; return true; }
        return false;
    }
}

// Usage: @Test(retryAnalyzer = RetryAnalyzer.class)

Quarantine Strategy

  • Tag flaky tests: @Tag("flaky") or TestNG group flaky
  • Exclude from blocking suites: @smoke and not @flaky
  • Run quarantined tests in separate non-blocking nightly job
  • Track fix progress—flaky tests must have assigned owner and deadline

Monitoring

  • Track flaky rate: (tests that passed on retry) / (total tests) per build
  • Jenkins test trend + custom dashboard (Grafana, ReportPortal)
  • Alert when flaky rate exceeds 2%—indicates infrastructure or test design problem
Never permanently leave retry on smoke tests to "keep CI green." Fix root cause or quarantine.

Test Data Management in CI/CD

Data Seeding Before Tests

stage('Seed Test Data') {
    steps {
        bat 'mvn exec:java -Dexec.mainClass=com.app.utils.TestDataSeeder -Denv=qa'
    }
}

Database Reset Between Runs

  • Run SQL reset script in pre-test stage
  • Use Docker compose to spin fresh DB container per pipeline run
  • Call API setup endpoint: POST /api/test/reset (test env only)

Environment-Specific Data Files

# Jenkins passes env; framework loads matching config
src/test/resources/testdata/qa/users.json
src/test/resources/testdata/staging/users.json

# Maven: -Denv=qa → framework loads testdata/qa/*.json
StrategyProsConsBest For
Static JSON/CSV filesSimple, version-controlledStale data, collisions in parallelSmoke, API tests
Dynamic seeding (API/DB)Fresh data every runSlower setup stageRegression, data-dependent flows
Data factory (Faker)Unique data per testHarder to assert specific statesParallel UI tests
Dedicated CI test accountsPredictable login statesAccount lockout riskAuth flows, role-based tests

Pipeline Strategy Summary

┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │ CI/CD TEST PYRAMID │ ├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤ │ PR (5 min) │ smoke.xml │ BLOCK on fail │ │ Post-Merge (15m)│ smoke + api.xml │ NOTIFY on fail │ │ Nightly (2 hr) │ regression.xml │ TICKET on fail │ │ Weekly (3 hr) │ crossbrowser.xml │ REPORT on fail │ │ Release (30 m) │ sanity + UAT │ BLOCK release │ └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Interview Questions

  1. Q: What tests should run on every PR?
    A: Smoke suite only—critical paths, under 10 min, blocks merge on failure. Never full regression on PR.
  2. Q: Explain build promotion with quality gates.
    A: Dev → smoke pass → deploy QA → regression pass → staging → UAT pass → production. Each gate has pass criteria.
  3. Q: What is a quality gate?
    A: Automated checkpoint (e.g., 95% pass rate, all smoke pass, 80% coverage) that must pass before promoting build.
  4. Q: How do you handle flaky tests in CI?
    A: Quarantine with @flaky tag, exclude from blocking suites, run in separate job, track flaky rate, fix root cause—never permanently retry on smoke.
  5. Q: Difference between smoke, sanity, and regression?
    A: Smoke = minimal critical paths (PR). Sanity = module/post-deploy checks. Regression = full coverage (nightly).
  6. Q: How to manage test data in parallel CI runs?
    A: Dynamic data factories (Faker), unique accounts per thread, DB reset before suite, or isolated Docker DB per pipeline.
  7. Q: When should CI block vs notify on test failure?
    A: Block: PR smoke, release UAT. Notify: nightly regression, weekly cross-browser—still important but not merge/release blocking.
  8. Q: How to design suites for fast feedback?
    A: Tier tests: smoke (20 tests, 5 min) → API (50 tests, 10 min) → regression (500 tests, 2 hr). Match trigger to tier.
  9. Q: What is test quarantine?
    A: Moving flaky tests to a separate non-blocking suite until fixed; excluded from smoke/regression gates via tags.
  10. Q: How do you enforce 95% pass rate in Jenkins?
    A: Parse JUnit results in pipeline script; calculate passCount/totalCount; call error() if below threshold.

Real Project Example

An ERP product team implemented a 5-tier strategy: PR smoke (15 tests, 4 min, blocks merge), post-merge API+smoke (15 min), nightly regression (420 tests, 90 min), weekly cross-browser (3 browsers), release sanity (30 tests before prod). Flaky tests tagged @flaky moved to quarantine job—flaky rate dropped from 8% to 1.5% in 6 weeks. Test data seeded via API before regression; static JSON for smoke. Quality gate: 100% smoke + 95% regression pass rate required for staging promotion.

Common Mistakes

  • Running full regression on every PR—developers ignore CI due to 1-hour wait
  • No test tier differentiation—same suite for PR and nightly
  • Ignoring flaky tests by adding retries everywhere—masks real issues
  • Shared test accounts across parallel runs—random login failures
  • No quality gates on staging/production promotion—bugs reach users
  • Static test data never refreshed—tests pass but validate outdated behavior

Troubleshooting Tips

  • Smoke suite too slow: Audit test count; move non-critical tests to post-merge or API suite.
  • High flaky rate: Identify top 10 flaky tests from retry logs; quarantine and assign owners.
  • Data collisions in parallel: Switch to dynamic data factory; never share user accounts across threads.
  • Quality gate false positives: Exclude quarantined @flaky tests from pass rate calculation.
  • Nightly always red: Team stops caring—fix top failures first; split environment issues from real bugs.

Quick Revision Notes

  • PR = smoke (5 min, block) | Nightly = regression (2 hr, notify)
  • Suites: smoke.xml, api.xml, regression.xml, crossbrowser.xml, sanity.xml
  • Promotion: smoke → QA → regression → staging → UAT → prod
  • Gates: 100% smoke, 95% pass rate, 80% coverage, 0 P1/P2 failures
  • Flaky: quarantine @flaky, separate job, track rate, fix root cause
  • Test data: seed before run, reset DB, env-specific files, dynamic factories for parallel

Section 15: Reporting in Jenkins

As an automation engineer, your tests are only as valuable as the reports stakeholders can read. Jenkins reporting turns raw test execution into actionable dashboards, trend graphs, and shareable artifacts that QA leads, developers, and managers rely on daily.

TestNG Default Reports

When you run TestNG via Maven Surefire, reports are auto-generated without any Jenkins plugin configuration.

test-output/ Folder

After every TestNG run, Maven creates target/surefire-reports/ (JUnit XML) and TestNG creates test-output/ with HTML files. Key files:

  • index.html — main dashboard with suite summary
  • emailable-report.html — lightweight summary designed for email sharing
  • testng-results.xml — machine-readable results for Jenkins plugins
  • testng-failed.xml — failed test methods for re-run
Automation Engineer Tip: Always configure Surefire to output JUnit XML format. Jenkins natively understands JUnit XML via the JUnit plugin — this is your baseline reporting layer even before Allure or Extent.

emailable-report.html

TestNG generates this automatically. Share it via Jenkins Email Extension Plugin using attachmentsPattern: 'test-output/emailable-report.html'. It contains pass/fail counts, duration, and grouped results — perfect for quick stakeholder updates.

Jenkins TestNG Results Plugin

Install TestNG Results Plugin from Manage Jenkins → Plugins. Configure as a post-build action:

  1. Go to job configuration → Post-build Actions
  2. Add Publish TestNG Results
  3. Set report path: test-output/testng-results.xml or **/testng-results.xml

Benefits for automation engineers:

  • Trend graphs showing pass/fail history over builds
  • Test result diff between builds (new failures, fixed tests)
  • Drill-down into failed test methods with stack traces
  • Build stability metrics for flaky test identification
// Declarative Pipeline — TestNG Results
post {
    always {
        step([$class: 'Publisher',
              reportFilenamePattern: '**/testng-results.xml'])
        // Or using junit step (also works with TestNG XML)
        junit '**/testng-results.xml'
    }
}

Allure Reports

Allure is the industry standard for rich, interactive test reports. It captures steps, screenshots, logs, and severity — ideal for UI automation frameworks.

Dependencies

<!-- pom.xml -->
<dependency>
    <groupId>io.qameta.allure</groupId>
    <artifactId>allure-testng</artifactId>
    <version>2.27.0</version>
</dependency>
<!-- For Cucumber BDD -->
<dependency>
    <groupId>io.qameta.allure</groupId>
    <artifactId>allure-cucumber7-jvm</artifactId>
    <version>2.27.0</version>
</dependency>

Allure Annotations for Automation

@Epic("Checkout Module")
@Feature("Payment Processing")
public class PaymentTests {

    @Test
    @Severity(SeverityLevel.CRITICAL)
    @Description("Verify credit card payment completes successfully")
    public void testCreditCardPayment() {
        loginPage.open();
        checkoutPage.selectCreditCard();
        // steps auto-captured via @Step methods
    }

    @Step("Enter card number: {cardNumber}")
    public void enterCardNumber(String cardNumber) {
        paymentPage.enterCard(cardNumber);
    }
}

Jenkins Allure Plugin Setup

  1. Install Allure Jenkins Plugin
  2. Manage Jenkins → Global Tool Configuration → Allure Commandline → Add installation (e.g., Allure 2.27.0)
  3. In pipeline, publish results after test stage
stage('Reports') {
    steps {
        allure includeProperties: false,
              jdk: '',
              results: [[path: 'target/allure-results']]
    }
}

Allure Dashboard Features

  • Timeline — visualize test execution order and parallel runs
  • Graphs — status, severity, duration trends
  • Categories — group failures by Product Defects vs Test Defects
  • Retries — track flaky tests with retry history
  • Attachments — screenshots, HTTP logs, page source on failure

Extent Reports

Extent Reports provides beautiful HTML dashboards with charts. Popular in Selenium + TestNG frameworks where you want a standalone HTML file without Jenkins plugin dependency.

ExtentSparkReporter Setup

// ExtentManager.java
public class ExtentManager {
    private static ExtentReports extent;

    public static ExtentReports getInstance() {
        if (extent == null) {
            ExtentSparkReporter spark = new ExtentSparkReporter("reports/ExtentReport.html");
            spark.config().setDocumentTitle("Automation Report");
            spark.config().setReportName("Regression Test Results");
            spark.config().setTheme(Theme.DARK);
            extent = new ExtentReports();
            extent.attachReporter(spark);
            extent.setSystemInfo("Environment", System.getProperty("env", "QA"));
            extent.setSystemInfo("Browser", System.getProperty("browser", "chrome"));
        }
        return extent;
    }
}

TestNG Listener Integration

public class ExtentTestNGListener implements ITestListener {
    @Override
    public void onTestStart(ITestResult result) {
        ExtentTest test = ExtentManager.getInstance()
            .createTest(result.getMethod().getMethodName());
        ExtentTestManager.setTest(test);
    }

    @Override
    public void onTestFailure(ITestResult result) {
        ExtentTestManager.getTest().fail(result.getThrowable());
        // Attach screenshot on failure
        String screenshot = captureScreenshot(result.getName());
        ExtentTestManager.getTest().addScreenCaptureFromPath(screenshot);
    }

    @Override
    public void onFinish(ITestContext context) {
        ExtentManager.getInstance().flush();
    }
}

Register in testng.xml: <listener class-name="com.qa.listeners.ExtentTestNGListener"/>

Jenkins HTML Publisher Plugin

publishHTML([
    allowMissing: false,
    alwaysLinkToLastBuild: true,
    keepAll: true,
    reportDir: 'reports',
    reportFiles: 'ExtentReport.html',
    reportName: 'Extent Report',
    reportTitles: 'Automation Test Report'
])
Security Note: HTML Publisher serves reports on Jenkins. Ensure reports do not contain credentials, API keys, or PII captured in screenshots. Sanitize before publishing.

Cucumber Reports

For BDD frameworks, Cucumber generates JSON reports that Jenkins renders into feature/scenario breakdowns.

Generate Cucumber JSON

// @CucumberOptions in runner class
@CucumberOptions(
    features = "src/test/resources/features",
    glue = "com.qa.steps",
    plugin = {
        "pretty",
        "html:target/cucumber-reports/cucumber.html",
        "json:target/cucumber-reports/cucumber.json"
    }
)

Jenkins Cucumber Reports Plugin

  1. Install Cucumber reports plugin
  2. Post-build action → Publish cucumber test results
  3. JSON path: target/cucumber-reports/*.json

Dashboard shows:

  • Feature and scenario pass rate
  • Step-level failure breakdown with stack traces
  • Duration per scenario for performance analysis
  • Trend over builds for BDD coverage tracking
// Pipeline
cucumber buildStatus: 'UNSTABLE',
         fileIncludePattern: '**/cucumber.json',
         jsonReportDirectory: 'target/cucumber-reports',
         sortingMethod: 'ALPHABETICAL'

Report Comparison Table

CriteriaTestNG DefaultAllureExtentCucumber
Setup ComplexityNone (auto-generated)Medium (deps + annotations)Medium (listener setup)Low (JSON plugin config)
Visual QualityBasic HTML tablesExcellent (interactive UI)Very Good (charts, dark theme)Good (feature hierarchy)
Step-Level DetailMethod level only@Step annotations, attachmentsLog steps manuallyGiven/When/Then steps
Jenkins IntegrationTestNG/JUnit pluginAllure plugin (trend graphs)HTML Publisher pluginCucumber Reports plugin
Screenshot SupportManual HTML embedNative attachmentsBuilt-in screenshot APIVia hooks + Allure/Extent
Best ForQuick baseline reportingEnterprise UI automationStandalone HTML sharingBDD / Cucumber projects

Report Archiving Strategy

Automation engineers must define retention policies so Jenkins disk does not fill up while keeping enough history for trend analysis.

Keep Last N Builds

// Jenkinsfile — discard old builds
options {
    buildDiscarder(logRotator(
        numToKeepStr: '30',           // keep last 30 builds
        artifactNumToKeepStr: '10'    // keep artifacts for last 10
    ))
}

Archive Artifacts

post {
    always {
        archiveArtifacts artifacts: '''
            target/allure-results/**,
            reports/ExtentReport.html,
            test-output/emailable-report.html,
            screenshots/**,
            logs/**
        ''', allowEmptyArchive: true, fingerprint: true

        junit '**/surefire-reports/*.xml'
    }
}

Recommended Strategy for Automation Projects

  • Allure raw results — archived per build; Allure plugin generates report on-the-fly
  • Extent HTML — archive + HTML Publisher for inline viewing
  • Screenshots/logs — archive on failure only to save disk
  • External storage — push reports to S3/Azure Blob for long-term retention beyond Jenkins
Production Pattern: Use Allure for Jenkins dashboard trends + archive screenshots/logs as artifacts. Send emailable-report.html or Allure summary link via email on failure. This gives managers visibility without bloating Jenkins storage.

Interview Questions

  1. Q: What is the difference between TestNG's emailable-report.html and Allure report?
    A: emailable-report is a static HTML summary auto-generated by TestNG with basic pass/fail tables. Allure is a rich interactive report with steps, attachments, severity, trends, and categories — requires framework integration and the Allure Jenkins plugin.
  2. Q: How do you publish Allure reports in a Jenkins pipeline?
    A: Install Allure Commandline in Global Tool Configuration, add allure-testng dependency, generate results in target/allure-results during tests, then use the allure pipeline step with the results path.
  3. Q: What file format does Jenkins JUnit plugin consume?
    A: JUnit XML format. TestNG's testng-results.xml and Surefire's TEST-*.xml both work with the junit pipeline step.
  4. Q: How do you attach screenshots to Extent Reports on test failure?
    A: Implement an ITestListener, capture screenshot in onTestFailure(), and call test.addScreenCaptureFromPath(path) before flushing the report.
  5. Q: What is the purpose of the Cucumber JSON report?
    A: It is a machine-readable report consumed by the Jenkins Cucumber Reports plugin to render feature/scenario dashboards with step-level failure details and trend graphs.
  6. Q: How do you prevent Jenkins disk from filling up with reports?
    A: Configure buildDiscarder to keep last N builds, limit artifact retention, archive screenshots only on failure, and optionally offload long-term storage to S3 or similar.
  7. Q: Can you use multiple reporting tools in the same project?
    A: Yes. Common pattern: Allure for detailed Jenkins dashboard + Extent for standalone HTML + JUnit XML for Jenkins test result trends. They serve different audiences.
  8. Q: What Allure annotations do automation engineers use most?
    A: @Epic, @Feature (organization), @Severity (priority), @Description (test purpose), @Step (granular step logging in page objects).
  9. Q: Why is publishHTML allowMissing set to false?
    A: To fail the build if the report was not generated — this catches reporting pipeline breaks instead of silently showing empty report links.
  10. Q: How do you share test reports with non-Jenkins stakeholders?
    A: Email emailable-report.html as attachment, share archived Extent HTML via shared drive, or send Allure report zip exported from Jenkins build artifacts.

Real Project Example

In a Selenium + TestNG + Maven e-commerce automation project with 800+ tests:

  • Allure integrated with @Step in page objects; Jenkins Allure plugin shows trend graphs — team spotted 12 flaky tests over 2 weeks
  • JUnit XML via Surefire for Jenkins build health badge
  • Extent Report published via HTML Publisher for QA lead quick review
  • Archiving: last 20 builds kept, screenshots archived only on failure
  • Email: on failure, emailable-report.html + top 5 failure names sent to dev channel

Result: Mean time to identify regression dropped from 4 hours to 30 minutes because reports were centralized in Jenkins with historical comparison.

Common Mistakes

  • Not adding Allure listener or aspectjweaver agent — Allure results folder stays empty
  • Wrong report path in Jenkins plugin config (e.g., test-output vs target/surefire-reports)
  • Setting allowMissing: true on publishHTML — missing reports go unnoticed
  • Committing reports to Git instead of generating them in CI
  • Capturing screenshots on every step — bloated reports and slow execution
  • Not configuring buildDiscarder — Jenkins master disk fills within weeks
  • Using absolute paths in report config instead of workspace-relative paths

Troubleshooting Tips

  • Empty Allure report: Verify target/allure-results contains JSON files; check aspectjweaver in Surefire argLine
  • HTML Publisher shows 404: Confirm reportDir path relative to workspace; check reportFiles matches exact filename
  • TestNG plugin shows zero tests: Validate testng-results.xml exists and is not empty; check glob pattern
  • Cucumber report missing scenarios: Ensure JSON plugin is in @CucumberOptions and runner executed (not skipped)
  • Reports show stale data: Add clean step before test run; disable report caching
  • Trend graphs flat: Need minimum 2+ builds with published results; verify plugin records history

Quick Revision Notes

  • TestNG auto-generates test-output/ — emailable-report.html for email, testng-results.xml for Jenkins
  • Allure = richest reports; needs allure-testng + Allure Commandline + Jenkins Allure plugin
  • Extent = standalone HTML via ExtentSparkReporter + TestNG Listener + HTML Publisher
  • Cucumber JSON → Cucumber Reports plugin for BDD dashboards
  • Always publish JUnit/TestNG XML via junit step for build trends
  • Archive with buildDiscarder; keep artifacts for last N builds only
  • Production combo: Allure dashboard + email on failure + screenshot archive

Section 16: Email Notifications

Email notifications bridge the gap between Jenkins build results and team awareness. For automation engineers, timely alerts mean failed regression suites get triaged before the next deployment window closes.

Why Email Notifications Matter

  • Immediate feedback — team knows within minutes if nightly regression failed
  • Stakeholder visibility — managers receive pass/fail summary without logging into Jenkins
  • Audit trail — email history documents build health over releases
  • Actionable context — attach reports, include failure details and build links
  • Escalation path — different recipients for success vs failure vs unstable builds

Jenkins Email Extension Plugin (Email-ext)

The default Jenkins email notification is basic. Email Extension Plugin (email-ext) provides HTML templates, triggers, attachments, and recipient token expansion — essential for automation pipelines.

Installation and SMTP Configuration

  1. Manage Jenkins → Plugins → Install Email Extension Plugin
  2. Manage Jenkins → Configure System → Extended E-mail Notification
  3. Configure SMTP server settings (see examples below)
  4. Send test email to verify configuration

SMTP Settings Overview

SettingDescription
SMTP ServerMail relay hostname
SMTP Port465 (SSL), 587 (TLS), or 25 (unencrypted)
CredentialsUsername/password or app-specific password
SSL/TLSEnable based on provider requirements
Default RecipientsFallback team distribution list

Gmail SMTP Example

# Jenkins Configure System → Extended E-mail Notification
SMTP Server:    smtp.gmail.com
SMTP Port:      465
SSL:            Enabled
Username:       automation-bot@company.com
Password:       xxxx-xxxx-xxxx-xxxx  (Google App Password)
Default Suffix: @company.com
Important: Gmail requires App Passwords when 2FA is enabled. Regular account passwords will fail authentication. For production, use a dedicated service account or corporate SMTP relay — not personal Gmail.

Office 365 SMTP Example

SMTP Server:    smtp.office365.com
SMTP Port:      587
TLS:            STARTTLS Enabled
Username:       jenkins-notify@company.com
Password:       <service account password>
Authentication: Required

Email Triggers by Build Result

TriggerRecipientsContent
Build SuccessQA team, scrum channelSummary: pass count, duration, report link
Build FailureTeam lead + developers + QAFailure stage, console excerpt, report attachment
Test Failure (Unstable)QA teamFailed test names, screenshot links, Allure URL
First Failure After SuccessOn-call engineerRegression alert — previously green build now red
Fixed After FailureTeam leadConfirmation that regression is resolved

Pipeline Email Configuration

pipeline {
    agent any

    stages {
        stage('Test') {
            steps {
                bat 'mvn clean test'
            }
        }
    }

    post {
        success {
            emailext (
                subject: "BUILD SUCCESS: ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER}",
                body: """<h2>Build Passed</h2>
                        <p><strong>Job:</strong> ${env.JOB_NAME}</p>
                        <p><strong>Build:</strong> #${env.BUILD_NUMBER}</p>
                        <p><strong>Duration:</strong> ${currentBuild.durationString}</p>
                        <p><strong>Branch:</strong> ${env.BRANCH_NAME ?: 'N/A'}</p>
                        <p><a href='${env.BUILD_URL}'>View Build</a></p>
                        <p><a href='${env.BUILD_URL}allure'>Allure Report</a></p>""",
                to: 'qa-team@company.com',
                mimeType: 'text/html',
                attachmentsPattern: 'reports/*.html'
            )
        }
        failure {
            emailext (
                subject: "BUILD FAILED: ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER}",
                body: """<h2 style='color:red'>Build Failed</h2>
                        <p><strong>Job:</strong> ${env.JOB_NAME}</p>
                        <p><strong>Build:</strong> #${env.BUILD_NUMBER}</p>
                        <p><strong>Duration:</strong> ${currentBuild.durationString}</p>
                        <p><a href='${env.BUILD_URL}console'>Console Output</a></p>
                        <p>Please investigate immediately.</p>""",
                to: 'qa-team@company.com, lead@company.com, dev-team@company.com',
                mimeType: 'text/html',
                attachmentsPattern: 'test-output/emailable-report.html, screenshots/**'
            )
        }
        unstable {
            emailext (
                subject: "TESTS FAILED: ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER}",
                body: """<h2 style='color:orange'>Build Unstable — Test Failures</h2>
                        <p>Some tests failed. Review the report.</p>
                        <p><a href='${env.BUILD_URL}testReport'>Test Report</a></p>""",
                to: 'qa-team@company.com',
                mimeType: 'text/html'
            )
        }
        always {
            // Optional: cleanup notification temp files
        }
    }
}

Advanced: Groovy Email Templates
