Store reusable HTML templates in Jenkins → Extended Email → Default Content → Editable Email Templates. Reference with ${SCRIPT, template="my-template"} for consistent branding across all automation jobs.

Slack Notifications as Alternative

Email is formal; Slack is faster for dev teams. Many automation projects use both — Slack for immediate alerts, email for management summaries.

Slack Plugin Configuration

  1. Install Slack Notification Plugin
  2. Manage Jenkins → Configure System → Slack → Workspace + Credential (Bot Token)
  3. Create Jenkins credential with Slack Bot OAuth token
  4. Test connection to verify channel access
post {
    success {
        slackSend(
            channel: '#qa-automation',
            color: 'good',
            message: "✅ Build PASSED: ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER} (${currentBuild.durationString})\n<${env.BUILD_URL}|View Build>"
        )
    }
    failure {
        slackSend(
            channel: '#qa-alerts',
            color: 'danger',
            message: "❌ Build FAILED: ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER}\n<${env.BUILD_URL}console|Console Log>"
        )
    }
}

// Simple one-liner
slackSend channel: '#qa-alerts', message: "Build ${currentBuild.result}: ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER}"

Microsoft Teams Webhook Notifications

Teams uses Incoming Webhooks — no dedicated Jenkins plugin required. Use httpRequest or office365ConnectorWebhooks step.

// Using Office 365 Connector plugin
office365ConnectorWebhooks([
    webhooks: [[
        name: 'QA Team Webhook',
        url: 'https://outlook.office.com/webhook/xxxx',
        notifyBackToUser: false,
        notifySuccess: true,
        notifyFailure: true
    ]]
])

// Or raw HTTP POST with JSON card
post {
    failure {
        script {
            def payload = """
            {
                "@type": "MessageCard",
                "summary": "Build Failed",
                "themeColor": "FF0000",
                "title": "Jenkins Build Failed",
                "sections": [{
                    "facts": [
                        {"name": "Job", "value": "${env.JOB_NAME}"},
                        {"name": "Build", "value": "#${env.BUILD_NUMBER}"}
                    ]
                }],
                "potentialAction": [{
                    "@type": "OpenUri",
                    "name": "View Build",
                    "targets": [{"os": "default", "uri": "${env.BUILD_URL}"}]
                }]
            }"""
            httpRequest url: 'https://outlook.office.com/webhook/xxxx',
                          httpMode: 'POST',
                          contentType: 'APPLICATION_JSON',
                          requestBody: payload
        }
    }
}

Notification Strategy for Automation Engineers

Best Practice: Route notifications by severity. Smoke test failure → Slack #qa-alerts immediately. Nightly regression failure → email QA lead + Slack. Success → Slack summary only (avoid email noise). Production deployment gate failure → email + Teams + PagerDuty.
  • Do not email on every success — causes alert fatigue; use Slack or weekly digest
  • Always include BUILD_URL — one-click access to console and reports
  • Attach reports on failure only — keeps email size manageable
  • Use parameterized recipient lists — different emails per environment (QA vs prod)

Interview Questions

  1. Q: What is the difference between default Jenkins email and Email Extension Plugin?
    A: Default email sends plain text on fixed triggers with limited customization. Email-ext supports HTML bodies, attachments, per-trigger templates, recipient tokens, and pipeline emailext step with rich content.
  2. Q: How do you attach test reports to Jenkins notification emails?
    A: Use attachmentsPattern in emailext step, e.g., attachmentsPattern: 'reports/*.html, test-output/emailable-report.html'. Files must exist in workspace at post-build time.
  3. Q: What SMTP settings are required for Gmail in Jenkins?
    A: smtp.gmail.com, port 465, SSL enabled, valid username, and Google App Password (not regular password if 2FA is on).
  4. Q: When would you use Slack instead of email?
    A: For real-time team alerts where immediate visibility matters — failed smoke tests, broken CI pipeline. Slack reduces response time; email suits formal stakeholder reporting.
  5. Q: How do you send different emails for success vs failure in a pipeline?
    A: Use post { success { emailext(...) } failure { emailext(...) } unstable { emailext(...) } } blocks with different subjects, recipients, and bodies.
  6. Q: What is an unstable build in Jenkins and how do you notify for it?
    A: Unstable means build completed but tests failed (or quality gate degraded). Use the unstable post condition with emailext to alert QA with test report links.
  7. Q: How do you configure Teams notifications without a dedicated plugin?
    A: Create an Incoming Webhook in Teams channel, then POST a MessageCard JSON payload via httpRequest step or use Office 365 Connector plugin.
  8. Q: How do you prevent notification spam from frequent builds?
    A: Email only on failure/unstable, use Slack for success summaries, configure fix-failure-only triggers, and set quiet period on jobs triggered by every commit.
  9. Q: What environment variables are commonly used in email body templates?
    A: JOB_NAME, BUILD_NUMBER, BUILD_URL, BUILD_URL/console, BRANCH_NAME, currentBuild.durationString, currentBuild.result.

Real Project Example

A fintech QA team running 15 Jenkins jobs (smoke, regression, API, performance):

  • Smoke (every commit): Slack #ci-alerts on failure only — zero email
  • Nightly regression: Email to qa-lead@ + dev-leads@ with emailable-report.html attachment on failure; Slack summary on success
  • Pre-release full suite: Email + Teams webhook to release managers with Allure link
  • SMTP: Corporate Office 365 relay — no Gmail dependency

Outcome: Developer response time to smoke failures dropped to under 15 minutes. Email volume reduced 70% by eliminating success emails on frequent jobs.

Common Mistakes

  • Using personal Gmail without App Password — authentication silently fails
  • Hardcoding recipient emails in Jenkinsfile instead of job parameters or credentials
  • Sending email on every successful build — team ignores all notifications
  • Missing mimeType: 'text/html' — HTML renders as raw tags in inbox
  • attachmentsPattern path wrong — emails send without expected reports
  • Not testing SMTP after Jenkins upgrade — mail relay breaks unnoticed
  • Including sensitive data (passwords, tokens) in email body or attachments

Troubleshooting Tips

  • Emails not sending: Check Manage Jenkins → System Log; enable email-ext debug logging
  • Authentication failed: Verify credentials, App Password, and TLS/SSL port match provider docs
  • Empty attachments: Confirm files exist before post block runs; check glob pattern case sensitivity
  • Slack not posting: Verify bot token scope (chat:write), bot invited to channel
  • Teams webhook 400: Validate JSON payload schema for MessageCard format
  • Emails in spam: Configure SPF/DKIM on corporate domain; use internal SMTP relay

Quick Revision Notes

  • Email-ext plugin → HTML emails, attachments, pipeline emailext step
  • Gmail: smtp.gmail.com:465 SSL + App Password
  • Office 365: smtp.office365.com:587 STARTTLS
  • post { success/failure/unstable } for conditional notifications
  • Slack: slackSend with channel, color, message + BUILD_URL link
  • Teams: Incoming Webhook + JSON MessageCard
  • Failure → email + Slack; success → Slack only to avoid noise

Section 17: Jenkins Parameters

Parameters transform a static Jenkins job into a flexible automation launcher. Instead of editing code or creating duplicate jobs for every browser, environment, or test suite, automation engineers expose runtime choices that anyone on the team can use.

Why Parameterize Pipelines?

  • Flexible execution — run smoke on QA, full regression on staging from same job
  • Reusable pipeline — one Jenkinsfile serves dev, QA, and release teams
  • No code changes — switch browser, tags, or thread count without committing
  • Self-service for QA — manual "Build with Parameters" replaces asking automation engineers
  • Environment safety — explicit ENV parameter prevents accidental prod runs

Parameter Types

TypeGroovy SyntaxUse Case
Choicechoice(name: 'X', choices: ['a','b'])Dropdown — browser, environment, suite
Stringstring(name: 'X', defaultValue: 'val')Free text — tags, URL, thread count
BooleanbooleanParam(name: 'X', defaultValue: true)Toggle — headless mode, debug flag
Passwordpassword(name: 'X', defaultValue: '')Masked input — API keys (use credentials instead when possible)
Filefile(name: 'X')Upload — test data file, config override

Common Automation Parameters

pipeline {
    agent any

    parameters {
        choice(
            name: 'BROWSER',
            choices: ['chrome', 'firefox', 'edge'],
            description: 'Browser for UI tests'
        )
        choice(
            name: 'ENV',
            choices: ['qa', 'staging', 'prod'],
            description: 'Target environment'
        )
        choice(
            name: 'SUITE',
            choices: ['smoke', 'regression', 'sanity', 'full'],
            description: 'Test suite to execute'
        )
        string(
            name: 'TAGS',
            defaultValue: '@smoke',
            description: 'Cucumber tags filter'
        )
        booleanParam(
            name: 'HEADLESS',
            defaultValue: true,
            description: 'Run browser in headless mode'
        )
        string(
            name: 'THREADS',
            defaultValue: '3',
            description: 'Parallel thread count'
        )
        string(
            name: 'BASE_URL',
            defaultValue: 'https://qa.app.com',
            description: 'Application base URL override'
        )
    }

    stages {
        stage('Validate Parameters') {
            steps {
                script {
                    if (params.ENV == 'prod' && params.SUITE == 'full') {
                        input message: 'Confirm PROD full regression?', ok: 'Proceed'
                    }
                }
            }
        }
    }
}

Using Parameters in Pipeline Stages

stages {
    stage('Test') {
        steps {
            bat """
                mvn clean test ^
                  -Dbrowser=${params.BROWSER} ^
                  -Denv=${params.ENV} ^
                  -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=${params.SUITE}.xml ^
                  -Dthread.count=${params.THREADS} ^
                  -Dheadless=${params.HEADLESS} ^
                  -Dbase.url=${params.BASE_URL}
            """
        }
    }
    stage('Cucumber Tests') {
        when {
            expression { params.TAGS?.trim() }
        }
        steps {
            bat "mvn test -Dcucumber.filter.tags=\"${params.TAGS}\""
        }
    }
}
Access Syntax: In declarative pipeline steps use ${params.PARAM_NAME}. In scripted pipeline or script blocks, params.BROWSER also works. Environment variables from parameters require explicit mapping (see below).

Environment Variables

Built-in Jenkins Environment Variables

VariableDescriptionAutomation Use
BUILD_NUMBERCurrent build IDReport naming, screenshot folders
JOB_NAMEJob nameEmail subjects, Allure environment info
BUILD_URLBuild page URLNotification links
WORKSPACEJob workspace pathFile paths, report directories
NODE_NAMEAgent running the buildDebug agent-specific failures
BRANCH_NAMESCM branch (Multibranch)Conditional test execution
GIT_COMMITCurrent commit SHATraceability in reports

Custom Environment Block

environment {
    REPORT_DIR = 'target/reports'
    ALLURE_RESULTS = 'target/allure-results'
    // Map parameter to env var for shell steps
    TEST_ENV = "${params.ENV}"
    BUILD_TAG = "${env.JOB_NAME}-${env.BUILD_NUMBER}"
}

stages {
    stage('Test') {
        steps {
            echo "Running on environment: ${env.TEST_ENV}"
            echo "Reports at: ${env.WORKSPACE}/${env.REPORT_DIR}"
            bat "mvn test -Denv=${env.TEST_ENV}"
        }
    }
}

Passing Parameters Between Stages

Method 1: Environment Block (Preferred)

Define values once in environment {} — available to all stages automatically.

Method 2: Script Variables

stage('Setup') {
    steps {
        script {
            env.DYNAMIC_SUITE = params.SUITE == 'full' ? 'regression.xml' : "${params.SUITE}.xml"
        }
    }
}
stage('Test') {
    steps {
        bat "mvn test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=${env.DYNAMIC_SUITE}"
    }
}

Method 3: Stash/Unstash (Cross-Agent Data)

stage('Build on Agent A') {
    steps {
        stash name: 'test-config', includes: 'config/${params.ENV}.properties'
    }
}
stage('Test on Agent B') {
    agent { label 'selenium-grid' }
    steps {
        unstash 'test-config'
        bat 'mvn test -Dconfig.file=config/${params.ENV}.properties'
    }
}

Active Choices Plugin — Dynamic Parameters

The Active Choices Plugin renders parameter values dynamically based on other selections — powerful for automation engineers managing complex test matrices.

// Freestyle or Pipeline with Active Choices
// When ENV = 'qa'     → SUITE choices: smoke, sanity, regression
// When ENV = 'staging' → SUITE choices: smoke, full
// When ENV = 'prod'    → SUITE choices: smoke only

// Groovy script for Active Choices Reactive Parameter:
if (ENV.equals('prod')) {
    return ['smoke']
} else if (ENV.equals('staging')) {
    return ['smoke', 'full']
} else {
    return ['smoke', 'sanity', 'regression', 'full']
}

Use cases: load browser list from config file, populate test suite names from repo directory listing, filter tags based on environment.

Parameter Best Practices for Automation

  • Provide sensible defaultValue — job should work with zero input on first run
  • Add description to every parameter — self-documenting for QA self-service
  • Validate dangerous combos (prod + full regression) with input step
  • Never store secrets in string parameters — use Jenkins Credentials binding
  • Log parameter values at build start for debugging: echo "Params: ${params}"
  • Keep parameter count manageable — more than 8 parameters suggests job should be split

Interview Questions

  1. Q: Why parameterize Jenkins pipelines instead of creating separate jobs?
    A: One pipeline reduces maintenance — same Jenkinsfile, same plugins, same reporting. Parameters let teams run different configs without duplicating jobs or changing code.
  2. Q: What is the difference between params.X and env.X?
    A: params.X are user-supplied build parameters. env.X are environment variables (built-in or custom). Parameters must be explicitly mapped to env vars if needed in shell export context.
  3. Q: How do you run a parameterized pipeline manually?
    A: Click "Build with Parameters" on the job page. Jenkins renders the parameter form defined in the parameters block.
  4. Q: Can you add new parameters to an existing pipeline without losing history?
    A: Yes. Add parameters block to Jenkinsfile. First run after change may require "Build with Parameters" to initialize defaults. Existing build history is preserved.
  5. Q: How do you pass Cucumber tags as a parameter?
    A: Define string parameter TAGS with default '@smoke', pass to Maven: -Dcucumber.filter.tags="${params.TAGS}".
  6. Q: What is Active Choices Plugin used for?
    A: Dynamic parameter values that change based on other parameter selections — e.g., suite list changes when environment changes.
  7. Q: How do you share data between pipeline stages on different agents?
    A: Use stash/unstash for files, or store values in env variables (master only), or use external storage (S3, database).
  8. Q: How do you prevent accidental production test execution?
    A: Restrict prod in choice parameter, add input confirmation step when ENV=prod, use Jenkins RBAC to limit who can select prod.
  9. Q: What happens if you reference params before parameters block is defined?
    A: On first job run, parameters may be null until "Build with Parameters" initializes them. Use defaultValue in parameter definition to avoid null issues.
  10. Q: How do booleanParam values appear in Maven command line?
    A: As string 'true' or 'false' — pass directly: -Dheadless=${params.HEADLESS}. Java/TestNG reads as boolean system property.
  11. Q: Can file parameters be used in pipeline?
    A: Yes. Uploaded file lands in workspace. Reference path in test framework config. Useful for ad-hoc test data uploads by QA.

Real Project Example

A SaaS company unified 6 separate Jenkins jobs (chrome-smoke, firefox-smoke, qa-regression, staging-regression, etc.) into one parameterized pipeline:

  • Parameters: BROWSER, ENV, SUITE, HEADLESS, TAGS, THREADS
  • QA team uses "Build with Parameters" daily — no Jenkinsfile edits needed
  • Active Choices limits prod to smoke-only suite
  • Nightly cron trigger uses default parameters; manual runs override as needed

Result: 6 jobs → 1 job. Jenkinsfile maintenance reduced 80%. New QA hires onboarded to CI in one training session.

Common Mistakes

  • Forgetting defaultValue — first build fails with null parameter
  • Using params in triggers or options block where not yet available
  • Passing prod URL without confirmation gate — data corruption risk
  • Hardcoding suite XML name mismatch (smoke vs smoke.xml)
  • Not escaping special characters in string params for shell commands
  • Storing passwords in string/password params instead of Credentials
  • Too many parameters — confuses users; split into separate jobs

Troubleshooting Tips

  • Parameter not appearing: Pipeline must run once after adding parameters block to register them
  • params.X is null: Check defaultValue; ensure "Build with Parameters" was used
  • Maven not receiving property: Verify -D flag spelling matches @Parameters or system property name in framework
  • Stash/unstash fails: Stash size limit default 5MB — increase or archive selectively
  • Wrong suite runs: Add echo step logging all params at pipeline start for audit

Quick Revision Notes

  • parameters {} block: choice, string, booleanParam, password, file
  • Access via ${params.NAME} in steps
  • Built-in env: BUILD_NUMBER, JOB_NAME, BUILD_URL, WORKSPACE, NODE_NAME
  • Custom env: environment { VAR = 'value' } or map from params
  • Cross-stage data: environment block, script env.VAR, stash/unstash
  • Active Choices: dynamic dropdowns based on other selections
  • Always set defaultValue and description on every parameter

Section 18: Real-Time Pipeline Design

This section ties together everything an automation engineer needs: checkout, build, parallel browser tests, reporting, notifications, and deployment gates — in one production-grade Jenkinsfile you can adapt to real projects.

End-to-End Pipeline Architecture

GitHub Push → Webhook → Jenkins → Checkout → Build → Unit Tests
    → Smoke Tests (parallel: Chrome + Firefox) → API Tests
    → Regression → Reports → Email → Slack → Deploy

┌──────────┐    ┌─────────┐    ┌─────────┐    ┌──────────┐
│  GitHub  │───▶│ Webhook │───▶│ Jenkins │───▶│ Checkout │
│   Push   │    │ Trigger │    │  Master │    │   SCM    │
└──────────┘    └─────────┘    └─────────┘    └────┬─────┘
                                                    │
    ┌───────────────────────────────────────────────┘
    ▼
┌────────┐   ┌────────────┐   ┌─────────────────────────────┐
│ Build  │──▶│ Unit Tests │──▶│ Smoke Tests                 │
│  mvn   │   │   JUnit    │   │  ┌─────────┐  ┌──────────┐  │
│compile │   │            │   │  │ Chrome  │  │ Firefox  │  │
└────────┘   └────────────┘   │  └─────────┘  └──────────┘  │
                               └──────────────┬──────────────┘
                                              ▼
                               ┌──────────────┐   ┌────────────┐
                               │  API Tests   │──▶│ Regression │
                               └──────────────┘   └─────┬──────┘
                                                        ▼
                               ┌─────────────────────────────────────┐
                               │ Reports → Email → Slack → Deploy    │
                               │ Allure  │ emailext │ slackSend│ QA  │
                               └─────────────────────────────────────┘

Complete Production-Grade Jenkinsfile

pipeline {
    agent any

    tools {
        maven 'Maven-3.9'
        jdk 'JDK-17'
    }

    parameters {
        choice(name: 'ENV', choices: ['qa', 'staging'], description: 'Target environment')
        choice(name: 'SUITE', choices: ['smoke', 'regression', 'full'], description: 'Test suite')
        choice(name: 'BROWSER', choices: ['chrome', 'firefox'], description: 'Primary browser')
        booleanParam(name: 'HEADLESS', defaultValue: true, description: 'Headless mode')
        string(name: 'TAGS', defaultValue: '@smoke', description: 'Cucumber tags (optional)')
    }

    environment {
        REPORT_DIR = 'target/reports'
        ALLURE_RESULTS = 'target/allure-results'
        TEST_ENV = "${params.ENV}"
    }

    options {
        buildDiscarder(logRotator(numToKeepStr: '30', artifactNumToKeepStr: '10'))
        timeout(time: 120, unit: 'MINUTES')
        timestamps()
        disableConcurrentBuilds()
    }

    triggers {
        // Nightly regression at ~2 AM
        cron('H 2 * * *')
        // Poll SCM fallback (prefer webhook)
        // pollSCM('H/15 * * * *')
    }

    stages {
        stage('Checkout') {
            steps {
                checkout scm
                script {
                    echo "Building ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER} on ${env.NODE_NAME}"
                    echo "Parameters: ENV=${params.ENV}, SUITE=${params.SUITE}, BROWSER=${params.BROWSER}"
                }
            }
        }

        stage('Build') {
            steps {
                bat 'mvn clean compile -DskipTests'
            }
        }

        stage('Unit Tests') {
            steps {
                bat 'mvn test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=unit-tests.xml'
            }
            post {
                always {
                    junit '**/surefire-reports/TEST-*.xml'
                }
            }
        }

        stage('Smoke Tests') {
            when {
                expression { params.SUITE != 'regression' }
            }
            steps {
                bat """
                    mvn test ^
                      -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml ^
                      -Dbrowser=${params.BROWSER} ^
                      -Dheadless=${params.HEADLESS} ^
                      -Denv=${params.ENV}
                """
            }
        }

        stage('Parallel Browser Tests') {
            when {
                expression { params.SUITE == 'full' }
            }
            parallel {
                stage('Chrome Regression') {
                    steps {
                        bat 'mvn test -Dbrowser=chrome -Dheadless=true -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=regression.xml -Denv=${params.ENV}'
                    }
                }
                stage('Firefox Regression') {
                    steps {
                        bat 'mvn test -Dbrowser=firefox -Dheadless=true -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=regression.xml -Denv=${params.ENV}'
                    }
                }
            }
        }

        stage('Regression') {
            when {
                expression { params.SUITE == 'regression' }
            }
            steps {
                bat """
                    mvn test ^
                      -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=regression.xml ^
                      -Dbrowser=${params.BROWSER} ^
                      -Dheadless=${params.HEADLESS} ^
                      -Denv=${params.ENV}
                """
            }
        }

        stage('API Tests') {
            when {
                expression { params.SUITE == 'full' || params.SUITE == 'regression' }
            }
            steps {
                bat "mvn test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=api.xml -Denv=${params.ENV}"
            }
        }

        stage('Cucumber BDD') {
            when {
                expression { params.TAGS?.trim() && params.SUITE != 'smoke' }
            }
            steps {
                bat "mvn test -Dcucumber.filter.tags=\"${params.TAGS}\" -Denv=${params.ENV}"
            }
        }

        stage('Reports') {
            steps {
                allure includeProperties: false,
                      jdk: '',
                      results: [[path: "${ALLURE_RESULTS}"]]
                publishHTML([
                    allowMissing: false,
                    alwaysLinkToLastBuild: true,
                    keepAll: true,
                    reportDir: "${REPORT_DIR}",
                    reportFiles: 'ExtentReport.html',
                    reportName: 'Test Report'
                ])
            }
        }

        stage('Deploy to QA') {
            when {
                allOf {
                    branch 'main'
                    expression { params.ENV == 'qa' }
                    expression { currentBuild.result == null || currentBuild.result == 'SUCCESS' }
                }
            }
            steps {
                input message: 'Deploy to QA environment?', ok: 'Deploy'
                bat 'mvn deploy -DskipTests -Denv=qa'
                echo "Deployed build ${env.BUILD_NUMBER} to QA"
            }
        }
    }

    post {
        always {
            junit '**/surefire-reports/*.xml'
            archiveArtifacts artifacts: 'screenshots/**, logs/**', allowEmptyArchive: true
            cleanWs(cleanWhenNotBuilt: false, deleteDirs: true, disableDeferredWipeout: true)
        }
        success {
            emailext(
                subject: "PASSED: ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER}",
                body: """<h2>Build Passed</h2>
                         <p>Env: ${params.ENV} | Suite: ${params.SUITE}</p>
                         <p><a href='${env.BUILD_URL}allure'>Allure Report</a></p>""",
                to: 'team@company.com',
                mimeType: 'text/html'
            )
        }
        failure {
            emailext(
                subject: "FAILED: ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER}",
                body: """<h2>Build Failed</h2>
                         <p><a href='${env.BUILD_URL}console'>Console Log</a></p>""",
                to: 'team@company.com',
                mimeType: 'text/html',
                attachmentsPattern: 'test-output/emailable-report.html'
            )
            slackSend channel: '#qa-alerts', color: 'danger',
                      message: "Build Failed: ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER}"
        }
        unstable {
            slackSend channel: '#qa-alerts', color: 'warning',
                      message: "Tests Failed: ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER} — <${env.BUILD_URL}testReport|Report>"
        }
    }
}

Webhook Configuration — GitHub to Jenkins

  1. GitHub repo → Settings → Webhooks → Add webhook
  2. Payload URL: https://jenkins.company.com/github-webhook/
  3. Content type: application/json
  4. Events: Push events, Pull request events (optional)
  5. Jenkins job: Enable "GitHub hook trigger for GITScm polling" under Build Triggers
Multibranch Pipeline: For modern setups, use Multibranch Pipeline with Branch Source plugin. Jenkins auto-discovers branches, creates jobs per branch, and triggers on push via webhook — no manual job creation per branch.

Cron Triggers for Nightly Regression

triggers {
    cron('H 2 * * *')    // ~2 AM nightly full regression
    cron('H 8-18/4 * * 1-5')  // Every 4 hours weekdays — smoke
}

// Parameterized cron (requires Parameterized Scheduler plugin)
// triggers { parameterizedCron('0 2 * * * % SUITE=full; ENV=staging') }

The H (hash) distributes load — Jenkins spreads builds across the hour instead of all firing at exactly 2:00 AM.

Multi-Environment Pipeline Design

// Pattern: separate deploy/test stages per environment
stages {
    stage('Test QA') {
        steps {
            bat 'mvn test -Denv=qa -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml'
        }
    }
    stage('Promote to Staging') {
        when { branch 'main' }
        steps {
            input message: 'Run staging tests?', ok: 'Proceed'
            bat 'mvn test -Denv=staging -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=regression.xml'
        }
    }
    stage('Production Smoke') {
        when {
            allOf { branch 'main'; expression { params.ENV == 'prod' } }
        }
        steps {
            input message: 'Confirm PROD smoke test', ok: 'Run'
            bat 'mvn test -Denv=prod -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml'
        }
    }
}

Pipeline Shared Libraries

Extract reusable Groovy functions so 20 automation projects share the same reporting, notification, and test execution logic.

// vars/runAutomation.groovy (Shared Library)
def call(Map config) {
    bat """
        mvn clean test ^
          -Dbrowser=${config.browser} ^
          -Denv=${config.env} ^
          -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=${config.suite}.xml ^
          -Dheadless=${config.headless ?: true}
    """
}

// Jenkinsfile in project repo
@Library('qa-shared-lib') _
pipeline {
    stages {
        stage('Test') {
            steps {
                runAutomation(browser: params.BROWSER, env: params.ENV,
                              suite: params.SUITE, headless: params.HEADLESS)
            }
        }
    }
}

Shared library structure:

qa-shared-lib/
├── vars/
│   ├── runAutomation.groovy
│   ├── publishReports.groovy
│   └── sendNotifications.groovy
└── src/
    └── org/qa/PipelineUtils.groovy

Pipeline Design Principles for Automation Engineers

  • Fail fast — smoke before regression; compile before tests
  • Parallelize wisely — browser parallel for full suite; avoid overloading agents
  • Conditional stages — use when {} to skip irrelevant stages per parameter
  • Always publish results — post { always { junit ... } } even on failure
  • Clean workspace — prevent stale artifacts causing false passes
  • Timeout everything — hung Selenium tests should not block agents for hours
  • Human gates for prod — input step before production deploy or test

Interview Questions

  1. Q: Describe a production-grade CI pipeline for Selenium automation.
    A: Webhook-triggered checkout → compile → unit tests → smoke → parallel browser regression → API tests → Allure/Extent reports → JUnit publish → email/Slack on failure → optional deploy with input gate.
  2. Q: How do you run Chrome and Firefox tests in parallel in Jenkins?
    A: Use parallel {} block with separate stages, each running mvn test with -Dbrowser=chrome or firefox. Ensure sufficient agent executors.
  3. Q: What is the purpose of the when block in declarative pipeline?
    A: Conditionally execute stages based on branch, parameters, build result, or custom expression — e.g., skip smoke when SUITE=regression.
  4. Q: How do you configure GitHub webhook to trigger Jenkins?
    A: Add webhook URL https://jenkins/github-webhook/ in GitHub repo settings. Enable "GitHub hook trigger" in Jenkins job Build Triggers.
  5. Q: What does cron('H 2 * * *') mean?
    A: Run approximately at 2 AM daily. H hash spreads load across the hour to prevent all jobs firing simultaneously.
  6. Q: What are Jenkins shared libraries and why use them?
    A: Reusable Groovy code (vars/ and src/) shared across pipelines — DRY principle for reporting, notifications, and test execution steps.
  7. Q: How do you prevent concurrent builds from conflicting?
    A: options { disableConcurrentBuilds() } or throttle concurrent builds per agent label.
  8. Q: What goes in post { always {} } vs post { failure {} }?
    A: always runs regardless of result — JUnit publish, artifact archive, workspace cleanup. failure runs only on failure — alert emails, Slack.
  9. Q: How do you add a manual approval before deployment?
    A: Use input step: input message: 'Deploy?', ok: 'Proceed' — pipeline pauses until authorized user approves.
  10. Q: Why use buildDiscarder in options?
    A: Automatically delete old builds and artifacts to prevent Jenkins disk exhaustion while keeping recent history for trends.
  11. Q: How do you handle different test suites from one pipeline?
    A: Parameterize SUITE choice and use when {} blocks or dynamic surefire.suiteXmlFiles=${params.SUITE}.xml.

Real Project Example

Enterprise ERP automation — 1200 Selenium tests, 200 API tests, 4 environments:

  • Trigger: GitHub webhook on push to feature branches; cron nightly full regression on main
  • Pipeline: 55-line Jenkinsfile with shared library for runTests() and publishReports()
  • Parallel: Chrome + Firefox + Edge on staging nightly (3 agents)
  • Reports: Allure dashboard + JUnit trends; Slack #erp-qa on failure
  • Gate: Smoke must pass before merge (GitHub branch protection + Jenkins status check)

Release cycle improved: regression feedback within 45 minutes of code merge vs 24 hours with manual test runs.

Common Mistakes

  • No timeout — hung browser tests block agent indefinitely
  • Running full regression on every commit — slow feedback loop
  • Missing post { always { junit } } — no test results recorded on failure
  • Parallel stages without enough executors — parallel runs sequentially anyway
  • Webhook + pollSCM both enabled — duplicate builds
  • Hardcoded environment URLs instead of parameterized ENV
  • Skipping cleanWs — stale screenshots/reports cause confusion
  • Deploy stage without input gate on production

Troubleshooting Tips

  • Webhook not triggering: Check GitHub webhook delivery log; verify Jenkins URL reachable; confirm hook trigger enabled on job
  • Parallel stage one fails: Other parallel branches continue; overall stage fails — check Blue Ocean for branch-specific logs
  • Cron not firing: Verify cron syntax; check Jenkins master timezone; ensure job not disabled
  • Shared library not found: Configure library in Manage Jenkins → System → Global Pipeline Libraries
  • Input step hangs pipeline: Set timeout on input or configure approval timeout in Jenkins settings

Quick Revision Notes

  • Flow: Push → Webhook → Checkout → Build → Test (smoke → parallel → API) → Reports → Notify → Deploy
  • parameters + when {} + parallel {} = flexible production pipeline
  • triggers { cron('H 2 * * *') } for nightly regression
  • post { always/failure/success/unstable } for reports and notifications
  • Shared libraries: reusable Groovy in vars/ for DRY pipelines
  • GitHub webhook URL: /github-webhook/ + enable hook trigger on job
  • buildDiscarder + timeout + disableConcurrentBuilds in options {}

Section 19: Jenkins Troubleshooting

Every automation engineer spends significant time debugging Jenkins failures. This section covers the top 10 issues with structured Problem → Root Cause → Investigation → Resolution → Prevention format — the same framework you should use in interviews and on real projects.

How to Debug Any Jenkins Failure

  1. Read console output — scroll to first red ERROR line, not the last
  2. Identify the failing stage — Blue Ocean or Stage View pinpoints stage
  3. Reproduce locally — run the same Maven command from console output on your machine
  4. Check recent changes — code, pom.xml, Jenkinsfile, plugin updates
  5. Check agent environment — Java version, browser, disk space on agent node

Issue 1: Build Failed — Compilation Error

AspectDetails
ProblemBuild fails at compile stage with Java syntax or dependency errors
Root CauseMissing dependencies, wrong Java version, code syntax error, incompatible library upgrade
InvestigationRead console output for [ERROR] lines; verify pom.xml dependencies; check Java version with java -version on agent; compare with local
ResolutionFix code/syntax; add missing dependency to pom.xml; configure correct JDK in Jenkins tools {} block; align Java version across team
PreventionPin JDK in Jenkinsfile tools {}; run compile in CI on every PR; use Maven enforcer plugin for Java version

Issue 2: Maven Build Failed

AspectDetails
ProblemMaven lifecycle fails — dependency download, plugin execution, or test phase errors
Root CauseDependency download failed, plugin version conflict, network/proxy issue, corrupt local .m2 cache
InvestigationRun mvn dependency:tree; check ~/.m2/repository for corrupt jars; verify proxy settings in settings.xml; test mvn clean install on agent manually
ResolutionDelete corrupt artifact from .m2 and rebuild; fix plugin version conflict; configure Jenkins Maven settings.xml with proxy/credentials; use internal Nexus/Artifactory mirror
PreventionCommit dependency versions explicitly; use corporate artifact repository; cache .m2 on agents with periodic cleanup
 
# Investigation commands
mvn dependency:tree -Dverbose
mvn clean install -X          # debug output
ls ~/.m2/repository/com/yourgroup/yourartifact/

Issue 3: Git Checkout Failed

AspectDetails
ProblemPipeline fails at checkout stage — cannot clone or fetch repository
Root CauseCredential expired/revoked, branch not found, repo URL changed, SSH key invalid, insufficient permissions
InvestigationVerify credentials in Jenkins Credentials store; check branch name spelling; test git clone <url> manually on agent; review GitHub/GitLab token expiry
ResolutionRegenerate and update credentials; fix branch name in Jenkinsfile; update repo URL; re-add SSH deploy key to repository
PreventionUse service account tokens with rotation calendar; use SSH keys with no passphrase for CI; monitor credential expiry alerts

Issue 4: Workspace Issues

AspectDetails
ProblemBuild fails with disk space, file lock, or stale workspace errors
Root CauseDisk full on agent, locked files from previous build, stale workspace with corrupted state
InvestigationCheck disk space: df -h (Linux) or Properties (Windows); look for "No space left on device"; check if previous build was killed mid-run
ResolutionWipe workspace: job page → Workspace → Wipe Out; add cleanWs step in pipeline; free disk space; delete old build artifacts
PreventionbuildDiscarder for old builds; cleanWs in post { always {} }; monitor agent disk with alerts; archive artifacts externally

Issue 5: Tests Pass Locally but Fail in Jenkins

AspectDetails
ProblemAutomation suite green on developer machine but red in Jenkins — most common automation engineer complaint
Root CauseHeadless mode missing, different browser/driver version, timing/flaky tests, different environment config, screen resolution, missing display
InvestigationCompare Java, browser, driver versions; check -Dheadless flag; review implicit/explicit waits; verify ENV-specific config; run Jenkins console command locally
ResolutionAdd -Dheadless=true; pin browser/driver versions in Jenkins agent; increase wait timeouts; use Docker for consistent environment; externalize config per ENV
PreventionRun tests in Docker locally and in CI; pin tool versions in Jenkinsfile; implement retry for known flaky tests; use explicit waits over Thread.sleep
Golden Rule: Copy the exact Maven command from Jenkins console output and run it locally. If it passes locally but fails in Jenkins, the difference is environment — not test logic.

Issue 6: Permission Denied

AspectDetails
ProblemAccess denied errors — cannot write files, execute scripts, or access Jenkins features
Root CauseJenkins user lacks OS file permissions, job not authorized for user, script security sandbox blocking Groovy
InvestigationCheck file ownership on agent; verify Jenkins user role (Job Configure, Build); review In-process Script Approval for pending signatures
Resolutionchmod/chown workspace directories; grant Jenkins role permissions; approve script in Manage Jenkins → In-process Script Approval
PreventionRun agents as dedicated jenkins user with consistent permissions; use least-privilege RBAC; avoid non-whitelisted Groovy methods

Issue 7: Port Already in Use

AspectDetails
ProblemJenkins fails to start or Selenium/Appium server cannot bind to port
Root CauseAnother Jenkins instance, zombie process, or conflicting service using port 8080/4444
InvestigationLinux: netstat -tlnp | grep 8080 or ss -tlnp | grep 8080; Windows: netstat -ano | findstr 8080
ResolutionKill conflicting process; change Jenkins HTTP port in /etc/default/jenkins or jenkins.xml; use different Selenium Grid port
PreventionDocument port assignments; use Docker with explicit port mapping; systemd service management for Jenkins

Issue 8: Agent Offline

AspectDetails
ProblemJenkins agent shows offline — builds queue indefinitely waiting for executor
Root CauseNetwork connectivity lost, agent Java not installed, SSH key expired, agent process crashed, firewall blocking JNLP port
InvestigationCheck agent log on agent machine; verify ping/SSH from master; check Manage Jenkins → Nodes → agent status and log; verify Java on agent
ResolutionRestart agent service; re-launch JNLP agent; regenerate SSH keys; open firewall ports; reinstall agent if corrupted
PreventionMonitor agent health with alerts; use permanent agent service (systemd/Windows Service); auto-reconnect JNLP agents

Issue 9: Plugin Failure

AspectDetails
ProblemJenkins UI errors, missing pipeline steps, or startup failure after plugin update
Root CauseIncompatible plugin version, missing dependency plugin, corrupt plugin install, Jenkins core/plugin version mismatch
InvestigationCheck Manage Jenkins → System Log; review plugin compatibility matrix; identify recently updated plugins; check /var/log/jenkins/jenkins.log
ResolutionRollback plugin to previous version; install missing dependency; remove corrupt plugin from $JENKINS_HOME/plugins and restart; upgrade Jenkins core if required
PreventionTest plugin updates on staging Jenkins first; use plugin BOM for known-good combinations; backup $JENKINS_HOME before updates

Issue 10: Out of Memory (OOM)

AspectDetails
ProblemJenkins master/agent crashes with java.lang.OutOfMemoryError; builds killed mid-execution
Root CauseLarge test suite memory footprint, too many parallel builds, memory leak in plugin, default JVM heap too small
InvestigationCheck JVM heap in Jenkins log; monitor memory during build; count concurrent builds; review Maven fork settings in Surefire
ResolutionIncrease heap: JAVA_OPTS="-Xmx2g -Xms512m" in jenkins.xml or systemd; limit concurrent builds; set Surefire forkCount appropriately; restart Jenkins periodically
PreventionRight-size agent machines; disableConcurrentBuilds on heavy jobs; use dedicated agents for large suites; monitor heap usage trends
 
# Jenkins JVM heap (Linux systemd)
# /etc/default/jenkins or override.conf
JAVA_ARGS="-Xmx2g -Xms512m -XX:+UseG1GC"

# Maven Surefire memory per fork
# pom.xml
<forkCount>2</forkCount>
<argLine>-Xmx1024m</argLine>

Jenkins Log Files — Locations and Usage

LogLocationWhen to Use
Build Console OutputJob → Build → Console OutputFirst stop for any failure — full command output
Jenkins System LogManage Jenkins → System LogPlugin errors, startup issues, webhook failures
jenkins.log/var/log/jenkins/jenkins.log (Linux)Master-level errors, OOM, plugin crashes
Agent LogManage Nodes → Agent → LogAgent connection, JNLP, SSH issues
Build Record$JENKINS_HOME/jobs/<job>/builds/<N>/logHistorical build log on disk
GC LogConfigured via -Xlog:gc*Memory leak investigation
Console Output is King: 90% of automation failures are diagnosed from the build console. Search for [ERROR], Exception, FAILED, and the first stack trace — not the summary at the bottom.

Interview Questions

  1. Q: Tests pass locally but fail in Jenkins — how do you troubleshoot?
    A: Copy exact Jenkins Maven command to local terminal. Compare Java/browser/driver versions. Check headless flag, environment config, and wait strategies. Run in Docker matching CI environment.
  2. Q: How do you fix "No space left on device" in Jenkins?
    A: Wipe workspace, configure buildDiscarder, delete old artifacts, archive to external storage, and monitor agent disk capacity.
  3. Q: Jenkins agent is offline — what steps do you take?
    A: Check agent log, verify network connectivity from master, confirm Java installed on agent, restart agent service, regenerate SSH/JNLP credentials if expired.
  4. Q: How do you investigate Maven dependency download failures?
    A: Run mvn dependency:tree, check .m2/repository for corrupt jars, verify proxy/settings.xml, test connectivity to Maven Central or internal Nexus.
  5. Q: What causes Jenkins OutOfMemoryError and how do you fix it?
    A: Default JVM heap too small for workload. Increase JAVA_OPTS -Xmx, limit parallel builds, tune Surefire forkCount, and investigate memory leaks via GC logs.
  6. Q: Git checkout fails with authentication error — what do you check?
    A: Jenkins Credentials for expired token/password, SSH key validity, repo URL correctness, and service account permissions on the repository.
  7. Q: Where do you look first when a Jenkins build fails?
    A: Build console output — find the first ERROR or exception in the failing stage. Then identify if it's compile, test, or infrastructure issue.
  8. Q: How do you handle plugin incompatibility after Jenkins upgrade?
    A: Check plugin compatibility matrix, rollback problematic plugins, update dependent plugins together, test on staging Jenkins before production upgrade.
  9. Q: How do you prevent workspace-related failures?
    A: Add cleanWs in post { always {} }, configure buildDiscarder, use disableConcurrentBuilds for jobs that lock resources.
  10. Q: What is In-process Script Approval in Jenkins?
    A: Security sandbox that blocks unapproved Groovy methods in pipelines. Admin must approve scripts at Manage Jenkins → In-process Script Approval when pipelines use restricted APIs.
  11. Q: How do you debug flaky tests that fail intermittently in CI?
    A: Review Jenkins test trend for pattern, increase explicit waits, run failed tests in isolation with retry, check parallel execution race conditions, capture screenshots/logs on failure.

Real Project Example

Nightly regression (900 tests) suddenly failed 100% in Jenkins but passed locally:

  • Investigation: Console showed ChromeDriver version 120 but Chrome browser updated to 122 on agent overnight (auto-update enabled)
  • Resolution: Pinned Chrome version via Docker agent; matched ChromeDriver in pom.xml using WebDriverManager
  • Prevention: Switched to Docker-based pipeline agents with pinned browser versions; disabled auto-update on test agents

Resolution time: 2 hours. Without structured troubleshooting (compare versions first), team estimated it would have taken 2 days.

Common Mistakes

  • Only reading the last lines of console output — root cause is usually earlier
  • Not reproducing with exact Jenkins command locally
  • Deleting .m2 entirely instead of targeted corrupt artifact removal
  • Updating all Jenkins plugins at once without staging test
  • Ignoring agent disk space until builds fail catastrophically
  • Increasing JVM heap without investigating memory leak root cause
  • Fixing symptoms (retry) without addressing flaky test root cause

Troubleshooting Tips

  • Keep a team runbook linking common errors to fixes — saves hours per incident
  • Use Blue Ocean timeline view to pinpoint failing parallel branch instantly
  • Add bat 'set' or sh 'env | sort' diagnostic stage to dump environment when debugging
  • Enable Maven -X debug temporarily — disable after fixing to reduce log noise
  • Compare last successful build console with failed build — diff reveals what changed
  • For agent issues, SSH to agent and run build commands manually as jenkins user

Quick Revision Notes

  • Debug order: Console output → failing stage → reproduce locally → check environment diff
  • Compilation: JDK version + pom.xml dependencies
  • Maven: dependency:tree, .m2 cache, proxy/Nexus
  • Git: credentials expiry, branch name, repo URL
  • Local pass / CI fail: headless, browser version, waits, ENV config
  • Agent offline: network, Java, SSH/JNLP key, restart agent
  • OOM: JAVA_OPTS -Xmx2g, limit concurrent builds, Surefire forkCount
  • Logs: Console Output (first), System Log (plugins), jenkins.log (master)

Section 20: Docker for Automation Engineers

Docker eliminates "works on my machine" by packaging your automation framework, browsers, and dependencies into portable containers. Every automation engineer should know enough Docker to run tests consistently in CI and locally.

What is Docker?

Docker is a containerization platform that packages applications with all dependencies into isolated, portable units called containers. Unlike VMs, containers share the host OS kernel — lightweight, fast to start, and identical everywhere.

Why Automation Engineers Use Docker

  • Consistent test environment — same Java, Maven, browser versions on every machine and CI agent
  • Selenium Grid in containers — spin up hub + Chrome + Firefox nodes with one command
  • Jenkins in container — portable CI server for team onboarding
  • Framework execution in container — run mvn test inside containerized environment
  • No "works on my machine" — if it passes in Docker, it passes everywhere
  • Parallel isolated runs — each container is a clean slate with no state leakage

Docker Core Concepts

ConceptDescriptionAutomation Analogy
ImageRead-only template with OS, Java, Maven, browsersLike a Java class — blueprint
ContainerRunning instance of an imageLike a Java object — live execution
DockerfileText file with build instructionsLike pom.xml — defines how to build
docker-composeMulti-container orchestration YAMLLike testng.xml — orchestrates multiple services
VolumePersistent storage mounted into containerStore test reports outside container
RegistryImage storage (Docker Hub, ECR)Like Maven Central for images

Essential Docker Commands for QA

# Run a container
docker run maven:3.9-eclipse-temurin-17 mvn --version
docker run -d --name my-grid selenium/standalone-chrome   # detached mode

# List running containers
docker ps
docker ps -a    # include stopped

# Manage containers
docker stop my-grid
docker start my-grid
docker restart my-grid
docker rm my-grid           # remove stopped container
docker rm -f my-grid        # force remove running

# View logs
docker logs my-grid
docker logs -f my-grid      # follow live logs

# Access container shell
docker exec -it my-grid bash
docker exec -it my-grid sh  # Alpine-based images

# Images
docker images
docker pull selenium/standalone-chrome:4.15.0
docker rmi image-name       # remove image
docker build -t my-automation:latest .   # build from Dockerfile

# Docker Compose
docker-compose up -d        # start all services in background
docker-compose down         # stop and remove containers
docker-compose logs -f hub  # follow hub logs
docker-compose ps           # service status

Dockerfile for Automation Framework

# Dockerfile — Selenium + Maven automation framework
FROM maven:3.9-eclipse-temurin-17

LABEL maintainer="qa-team@company.com"
LABEL description="Automation test runner"

WORKDIR /app

# Cache dependencies layer (rebuilds only when pom.xml changes)
COPY pom.xml .
RUN mvn dependency:resolve -B

# Copy framework source
COPY src ./src
COPY testng.xml .
COPY config ./config

# Create report directories
RUN mkdir -p reports screenshots target/allure-results

# Default: run smoke suite headless
CMD ["mvn", "clean", "test", \
     "-Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml", \
     "-Dheadless=true"]

# Build: docker build -t automation-framework:latest .
# Run:   docker run --rm -v $(pwd)/reports:/app/reports automation-framework:latest
# Override suite:
#        docker run --rm automation-framework:latest \
#          mvn test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=regression.xml

Build and Run Workflow

# Build image
docker build -t automation-framework:latest .

# Run with report volume mount (reports persist on host)
docker run --rm \
  -v "${PWD}/reports:/app/reports" \
  -v "${PWD}/screenshots:/app/screenshots" \
  -e ENV=qa \
  automation-framework:latest

# Run specific suite overriding CMD
docker run --rm automation-framework:latest \
  mvn test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=regression.xml -Dbrowser=firefox

Docker Compose for Selenium Grid

# docker-compose.yml — Selenium Grid 4
services:
  hub:
    image: selenium/hub:4.15.0
    container_name: selenium-hub
    ports:
      - "4444:4444"
      - "4442:4442"
      - "4443:4443"
    environment:
      - SE_SESSION_REQUEST_TIMEOUT=300
      - SE_NODE_SESSION_TIMEOUT=300

  chrome:
    image: selenium/node-chrome:4.15.0
    depends_on:
      - hub
    environment:
      - SE_EVENT_BUS_HOST=hub
      - SE_EVENT_BUS_PUBLISH_PORT=4442
      - SE_EVENT_BUS_SUBSCRIBE_PORT=4443
      - SE_NODE_MAX_SESSIONS=2
    shm_size: '2gb'    # prevent Chrome crash in container
    scale: 2           # docker-compose up --scale chrome=2

  firefox:
    image: selenium/node-firefox:4.15.0
    depends_on:
      - hub
    environment:
      - SE_EVENT_BUS_HOST=hub
      - SE_EVENT_BUS_PUBLISH_PORT=4442
      - SE_EVENT_BUS_SUBSCRIBE_PORT=4443
    shm_size: '2gb'

# Start: docker-compose up -d
# Grid UI: http://localhost:4444
# Test config: webdriver.remote.url=http://localhost:4444
shm_size: '2gb': Chrome crashes in Docker without adequate shared memory. Always set shm_size to at least 2gb for Selenium Chrome nodes — this is the #1 Docker + Selenium gotcha for automation engineers.

Jenkins + Docker Integration

Run each build inside a fresh Docker container — clean environment every time, no stale browser sessions or leftover files.

Docker Agent in Pipeline

pipeline {
    agent {
        docker {
            image 'maven:3.9-eclipse-temurin-17'
            args '-v /var/run/docker.sock:/var/run/docker.sock'
        }
    }
    stages {
        stage('Test') {
            steps {
                sh 'mvn clean test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml -Dheadless=true'
            }
        }
    }
}

Docker Agent with Selenium Sidecar

pipeline {
    agent none
    stages {
        stage('Grid Tests') {
            agent {
                docker {
                    image 'maven:3.9-eclipse-temurin-17'
                    args '--network=host'
                }
            }
            steps {
                sh '''
                    docker-compose -f docker-compose.grid.yml up -d
                    sleep 10
                    mvn test -Dgrid.url=http://localhost:4444 -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=regression.xml
                '''
            }
            post {
                always {
                    sh 'docker-compose -f docker-compose.grid.yml down'
                }
            }
        }
    }
}

Custom Automation Image in Jenkins

agent {
    docker {
        image 'company/automation-framework:2.1.0'
        registryUrl 'https://registry.company.com'
        registryCredentialsId 'docker-registry-credentials'
        reuseNode true
    }
}

Docker Best Practices for Automation

  • Layer caching — COPY pom.xml + dependency:resolve before COPY source — faster rebuilds
  • Volume mounts for reports — persist reports/screenshots outside container
  • Pin image versions — selenium/standalone-chrome:4.15.0 not :latest
  • .dockerignore — exclude target/, .git/, reports/ from build context
  • Multi-stage builds — separate build and test stages for smaller images
  • Non-root user — run tests as non-root for security in CI
# .dockerignore
target/
.git/
reports/
screenshots/
*.iml
.idea/

Interview Questions

  1. Q: What is the difference between a Docker image and container?
    A: Image is a read-only template (blueprint). Container is a running instance of that image. You build an image once, run many containers from it.
  2. Q: Why do automation engineers use Docker?
    A: Consistent test environments across local, CI, and staging. Eliminates version mismatches for Java, browsers, and drivers. Enables Selenium Grid and clean CI agents per build.
  3. Q: How do you run Selenium Grid with Docker?
    A: docker-compose with selenium/hub and selenium/node-chrome/node-firefox services. Connect tests via webdriver.remote.url=http://localhost:4444.
  4. Q: What is shm_size and why is it needed for Chrome in Docker?
    A: Shared memory allocation. Chrome requires significant shared memory; default 64MB causes crashes. Set shm_size: '2gb' in docker-compose for Chrome nodes.
  5. Q: How do you persist test reports from a Docker container?
    A: Volume mount: docker run -v $(pwd)/reports:/app/reports. Reports written inside container appear on host filesystem.
  6. Q: How do you use Docker as a Jenkins pipeline agent?
    A: agent { docker { image 'maven:3.9-eclipse-temurin-17' } } — Jenkins starts container, runs steps inside, destroys after build.
  7. Q: What is the purpose of COPY pom.xml before COPY src in Dockerfile?
    A: Docker layer caching. Dependencies resolve in a separate layer that only rebuilds when pom.xml changes — much faster subsequent builds.
  8. Q: docker run vs docker-compose up — when to use each?
    A: docker run for single containers (one-off test runs). docker-compose for multi-container setups (Selenium Grid hub + nodes).
  9. Q: How do you debug a failing test inside a Docker container?
    A: docker exec -it container-name bash to get shell access; docker logs container-name for output; run with interactive mode and override CMD.
  10. Q: What is docker-compose scale used for in Selenium Grid?
    A: Run multiple browser node instances: docker-compose up --scale chrome=3 — scales parallel browser capacity for faster test execution.
  11. Q: Why pin Docker image versions instead of using :latest?
    A: :latest changes unpredictably — browser version drift causes test failures. Pinning ensures reproducible builds across time and environments.

Real Project Example

Mobile banking automation team migrated from bare-metal Jenkins agents to Docker:

  • Before: Chrome auto-updated on agents overnight, breaking 30% of tests weekly
  • After: Custom Dockerfile with pinned Chrome 120 + ChromeDriver 120 + Maven 3.9 + JDK 17
  • Grid: docker-compose with 2 Chrome + 1 Firefox node; Jenkins pipeline agent uses docker {} block
  • Reports: Volume mount persists Allure results to host; Jenkins archives as artifacts

Result: Environment-related failures dropped from ~30% to zero. New team member onboarding: docker-compose up + mvn test — running in 10 minutes.

Common Mistakes

  • Using :latest tag — unpredictable browser version changes break tests
  • Forgetting shm_size for Chrome — random browser crashes in container
  • Not mounting volumes — reports lost when container stops
  • COPY . . before dependency resolve — slow rebuilds, no layer caching
  • Running as root in container — security risk in shared CI infrastructure
  • Not adding .dockerignore — large build context slows docker build
  • Exposing Grid port 4444 publicly without authentication — security vulnerability

Troubleshooting Tips

  • Chrome crash in container: Add shm_size: '2gb'; increase container memory limit
  • Cannot connect to Grid: Verify hub is running (docker ps); check network mode; use service name not localhost in compose network
  • Permission denied on volume mount: Match container user UID with host directory ownership
  • Image build slow: Optimize layer order; use .dockerignore; leverage build cache
  • docker: not found in Jenkins: Install Docker on agent; add jenkins user to docker group; mount docker.sock
  • Tests pass in container locally but fail in Jenkins: Check Jenkins docker agent args and network configuration

Quick Revision Notes

  • Image = template; Container = running instance; Dockerfile = build instructions
  • Key commands: run, ps, logs, exec -it, build -t, compose up -d
  • Dockerfile: FROM maven → COPY pom.xml → dependency:resolve → COPY src → CMD mvn test
  • Selenium Grid: docker-compose hub + chrome + firefox; shm_size 2gb for Chrome
  • Jenkins: agent { docker { image '...' } } for clean per-build environment
  • Volume mount (-v) to persist reports outside container
  • Pin image versions; never use :latest in CI

Section 21: Kubernetes Overview for Automation Engineers

You do not need to be a Kubernetes administrator — but as an SDET, you should understand K8s architecture because the applications you test, the grids you use, and the CI pipelines you maintain increasingly run on Kubernetes.

What is Kubernetes?

Kubernetes (K8s) is an open-source container orchestration platform that automates deployment, scaling, and management of containerized applications. It manages hundreds of containers across clusters of machines — handling failures, scaling, networking, and rollouts automatically.

Why SDETs Should Know Kubernetes

  • Application under test runs on K8s — understand deployment failures to triage environment vs product bugs
  • Selenium Grid on K8s — scale browser nodes dynamically based on test queue depth
  • Jenkins on K8s — dynamic build agents as pods; each build gets clean environment
  • Deployment failures are QA responsibility — "tests fail after deploy" often means pod crash, not test bug
  • Test environment management — spin up isolated QA namespaces per feature branch
  • Interview expectation — K8s basics increasingly asked for senior automation roles

Key Kubernetes Concepts — QA Perspective

ConceptSimple ExplanationQA Relevance
PodSmallest deployable unit; runs one or more containersLike one test runner instance — check if it's running before blaming tests
DeploymentManages pod replicas; handles rolling updatesLike scaling Selenium Grid nodes — 3 Chrome pods for parallel runs
ServiceStable network endpoint for pods; load balancingAccess application URL consistently even when pods restart
NamespaceVirtual cluster for isolationSeparate qa, staging, prod environments in one cluster
ConfigMapStores non-sensitive configurationTest environment configs — base URLs, feature flags
SecretStores sensitive data (encrypted at rest)API keys, DB passwords for test data setup
IngressExternal HTTP/HTTPS access to servicesRoute qa.app.com to QA namespace service
NodePhysical or virtual machine in clusterWhere pods actually run — node failure kills pods on it
 
Kubernetes Cluster (QA View)
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  Namespace: qa                                          │
│  ┌──────────────┐  ┌──────────────┐  ┌──────────────┐  │
│  │ Pod: app-1   │  │ Pod: app-2   │  │ Pod: app-3   │  │
│  │ (app under   │  │ (replica)    │  │ (replica)    │  │
│  │  test)       │  │              │  │              │  │
│  └──────┬───────┘  └──────┬───────┘  └──────┬───────┘  │
│         └─────────────────┼─────────────────┘          │
│                           │                             │
│                    ┌──────▼──────┐                      │
│                    │  Service    │ ← qa-app-service     │
│                    │  (ClusterIP)│   stable endpoint    │
│                    └──────┬──────┘                      │
│                           │                             │
│  ┌──────────────┐  ┌──────▼──────┐  ┌──────────────┐  │
│  │ Pod: chrome  │  │ Pod: hub    │  │ Pod: firefox │  │
│  │ (Grid node)  │  │ (Grid hub)  │  │ (Grid node)  │  │
│  └──────────────┘  └─────────────┘  └──────────────┘  │
│         Selenium Grid Deployment (scales with KEDA)    │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Essential kubectl Commands for QA

# Check application status
kubectl get pods                          # all pods in default namespace
kubectl get pods -n qa                    # pods in qa namespace
kubectl get pods -n qa -w                 # watch live status changes

# View application logs (critical for triaging test failures)
kubectl logs pod-name -n qa
kubectl logs pod-name -n qa --tail=100    # last 100 lines
kubectl logs pod-name -n qa -f              # follow live logs
kubectl logs deployment/app-name -n qa      # logs from deployment

# Detailed pod information (events, restarts, errors)
kubectl describe pod pod-name -n qa
# Look for: Events section, Restart Count, State: Waiting/CrashLoopBackOff

# Access running pod (debug inside container)
kubectl exec -it pod-name -n qa -- bash
kubectl exec -it pod-name -n qa -- curl localhost:8080/health

# Find service endpoints (application URLs)
kubectl get services -n qa
kubectl get ingress -n qa

# Check deployments and rollout status
kubectl get deployments -n qa
kubectl rollout status deployment/app-name -n qa

# Scale Selenium Grid nodes
kubectl scale deployment/chrome-node --replicas=5 -n qa

# Port forward for local access to cluster service
kubectl port-forward svc/qa-app-service 8080:80 -n qa
# Access app at http://localhost:8080

# ConfigMaps and Secrets (test environment config)
kubectl get configmaps -n qa
kubectl describe configmap app-config -n qa
kubectl get secrets -n qa

QA Troubleshooting with kubectl

When tests fail after a deployment, check infrastructure before re-running tests:

# Step 1: Are pods running?
kubectl get pods -n qa
# STATUS should be Running, RESTARTS should be 0 (or low)

# Step 2: Any CrashLoopBackOff or Error?
kubectl describe pod failing-pod -n qa
# Check Events: "Back-off restarting failed container"

# Step 3: What do application logs say?
kubectl logs failing-pod -n qa --previous   # logs from crashed container

# Step 4: Can service be reached?
kubectl get svc -n qa
kubectl exec -it any-running-pod -n qa -- curl http://qa-app-service/health

# Step 5: Did config change?
kubectl describe configmap app-config -n qa
QA Triage Rule: If kubectl get pods shows CrashLoopBackOff or Error status, the test failure is an environment issue — not a product bug. Escalate to DevOps with pod describe output attached.

Selenium Grid on Kubernetes

Running Selenium Grid on K8s enables dynamic scaling — spin up browser nodes when tests queue, scale down when idle.

  • KEDA (Kubernetes Event-Driven Autoscaling) — scales Grid nodes based on session queue length
  • Moon ( Aerokube ) — commercial Selenium Grid operator for K8s with built-in VNC, video recording
  • Selenoid — lightweight Grid alternative with K8s deployment options
  • Selenium Grid 4 Helm Chart — official chart for hub + node deployment on K8s
# Simplified Selenium Grid Deployment on K8s
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: chrome-node
  namespace: qa
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: chrome-node
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: chrome-node
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: chrome
        image: selenium/node-chrome:4.15.0
        env:
        - name: SE_EVENT_BUS_HOST
          value: selenium-hub
        resources:
          limits:
            memory: "2Gi"
            cpu: "1"

Jenkins on Kubernetes

The Kubernetes Plugin for Jenkins creates dynamic build agents as pods — each pipeline run gets a fresh pod with specified container image, destroyed after completion.

// Jenkinsfile with Kubernetes dynamic agent
pipeline {
    agent {
        kubernetes {
            yaml '''
                apiVersion: v1
                kind: Pod
                spec:
                  containers:
                  - name: maven
                    image: maven:3.9-eclipse-temurin-17
                    command: ["sleep"]
                    args: ["99999"]
                    resources:
                      limits:
                        memory: "2Gi"
                        cpu: "1"
            '''
        }
    }
    stages {
        stage('Test') {
            steps {
                container('maven') {
                    sh 'mvn clean test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xml'
                }
            }
        }
    }
}

Benefits for automation engineers:

  • Each build gets isolated pod — no stale browser sessions or leftover files
  • Scale agents automatically — 10 parallel builds = 10 pods
  • Define exact container image per pipeline — Maven, Python, Node as needed
  • Resource limits prevent one heavy test suite from starving others

K8s Knowledge Level for Automation Engineers

Target Skill Level: Not deep ops — but understand architecture, read pod status, pull logs, exec into containers, and know when a test failure is infrastructure vs application. Senior SDETs should be able to deploy a test Grid on Minikube locally.
SkillJunior SDETSenior SDETNot Required
kubectl get pods/logsRequiredRequired—
Read pod describe outputRequiredRequired—
Port-forward for local testingNice to haveRequired—
Deploy Grid on MinikubeNice to haveRequired—
Write K8s YAML manifestsNot requiredBasicAdvanced operators
Cluster administrationNot requiredNot requiredDevOps team
Helm chart customizationNot requiredBasicChart development

Interview Questions

  1. Q: What is Kubernetes and why should automation engineers know it?
    A: Container orchestration platform managing deployment, scaling, and networking of containers. SDETs need it because apps under test, Selenium Grid, and Jenkins agents increasingly run on K8s — understanding pod status and logs helps triage test failures.
  2. Q: What is a Pod in Kubernetes?
    A: Smallest deployable unit — one or more containers sharing network and storage. For QA: if pod is CrashLoopBackOff, tests will fail regardless of test code quality.
  3. Q: How do you check if the application is running before running tests?
    A: kubectl get pods -n qa (STATUS=Running), kubectl logs pod-name, curl health endpoint via port-forward or service URL.
  4. Q: What kubectl command shows why a pod is failing?
    A: kubectl describe pod pod-name — Events section shows OOMKilled, ImagePullBackOff, CrashLoopBackOff with reasons.
  5. Q: How does Selenium Grid scale on Kubernetes?
    A: Grid nodes run as Deployment replicas. KEDA autoscales based on session queue. Scale manually with kubectl scale deployment --replicas=N.
  6. Q: How does Jenkins use Kubernetes for dynamic agents?
    A: Kubernetes plugin creates a pod per build with specified container image. Pod destroyed after build — clean environment every time.
  7. Q: What is a Namespace and how is it used in testing?
    A: Virtual cluster providing isolation. QA namespace separate from staging/prod — safe to run destructive tests without affecting other environments.
  8. Q: What is the difference between ConfigMap and Secret?
    A: ConfigMap stores non-sensitive config (URLs, feature flags). Secret stores sensitive data (passwords, API keys) base64-encoded. Both inject env vars into pods.
  9. Q: Tests fail after deployment — how do you determine if it's K8s or application issue?
    A: kubectl get pods (check STATUS), kubectl logs (app errors), kubectl describe pod (Events). If pods healthy and logs clean, it's likely a test or app logic issue.
  10. Q: What K8s knowledge level is expected from automation engineers?
    A: Basic: kubectl get/describe/logs/exec, understand pod/deployment/service/namespace concepts. Not expected: cluster admin, writing operators, network policy configuration.

Real Project Example

E-commerce platform — application and test infrastructure both on AWS EKS:

  • App under test: 3 replicas in staging namespace; tests hit service URL not pod IP
  • Selenium Grid: KEDA-scaled Chrome nodes — 0 nodes idle, 5 nodes during nightly regression
  • Jenkins: Dynamic agents on K8s — each build gets maven:3.9 pod, destroyed after 30 min
  • QA triage: When regression failed after deploy, SDET ran kubectl get pods, found ImagePullBackOff — new Docker image tag typo in deployment YAML, not a test issue
  • Per-branch testing: Feature branches get dedicated namespace with ConfigMap pointing to branch-specific service URL

SDET kubectl skills saved 4 hours of unnecessary test re-runs and false bug reports per release cycle.

Common Mistakes

  • Running tests against pod IP instead of Service URL — pod restarts change IP
  • Ignoring CrashLoopBackOff and re-running tests hoping they pass
  • Not specifying namespace (-n qa) — checking wrong environment's pods
  • Assuming test failure is always application bug — missing K8s infrastructure check
  • Not checking application logs before escalating test failures to developers
  • Over-provisioning Grid nodes without KEDA — paying for idle browser pods 24/7

Troubleshooting Tips

  • Pod CrashLoopBackOff: kubectl logs pod --previous for crash reason; check describe Events
  • ImagePullBackOff: Wrong image tag or missing registry credentials — check deployment YAML
  • OOMKilled: Pod exceeded memory limit — increase resources.limits.memory in deployment
  • Tests timeout connecting to app: Verify service exists (kubectl get svc); check Ingress rules
  • Grid sessions queue indefinitely: kubectl get pods for grid nodes; scale up if pending
  • Local access to cluster app: kubectl port-forward svc/app-service 8080:80 -n qa

Quick Revision Notes

  • K8s = container orchestration; SDETs need basics not admin skills
  • Pod = smallest unit; Deployment = manages replicas; Service = stable endpoint
  • Namespace = environment isolation (qa, staging, prod)
  • ConfigMap = config; Secret = sensitive data
  • Key commands: get pods, logs, describe pod, exec -it, get svc, port-forward
  • CrashLoopBackOff/ImagePullBackOff = environment issue, not test bug
  • Selenium Grid on K8s: KEDA autoscaling, Moon/Selenoid alternatives
  • Jenkins on K8s: dynamic agent pods via Kubernetes plugin — clean per-build environment

Section 22: Cloud CI/CD for Automation Engineers

As an automation engineer, cloud CI/CD platforms are where your test suites become gatekeepers for every merge, deployment, and release. You do not just "run tests in the cloud" — you design pipelines that trigger on the right events, execute the right suite against the right environment, publish actionable reports, and fail fast when quality drops. This section covers Azure DevOps, GitHub Actions, and GitLab CI from a hands-on automation perspective, plus a platform comparison and decision guide.

Azure DevOps Pipelines

What It Is

Azure DevOps Pipelines is Microsoft's cloud-native CI/CD service, tightly integrated with Azure Repos, GitHub, and Azure Test Plans. For automation engineers, it provides YAML-defined pipelines, hosted agents (Windows, Linux, macOS), artifact storage, test result publishing, and PR validation — all without maintaining Jenkins infrastructure.

Automation Engineer Takeaway: Azure DevOps excels when your organization already uses Microsoft tooling (Azure, .NET, Visual Studio). Test Plans integration lets you link automated runs to manual test cases — valuable for regulated industries and audit trails.

Pipeline YAML Structure

Azure Pipelines use azure-pipelines.yml at the repo root. Key concepts: trigger (branches/events), pool (agent OS), steps (tasks), and variables.

trigger:
  - main
  - develop

pr:
  branches:
    include:
      - main

pool:
  vmImage: 'ubuntu-latest'

variables:
  MAVEN_OPTS: '-Xmx1024m'
  SUITE_FILE: 'smoke.xml'

steps:
  - task: Maven@3
    displayName: 'Run Automation Suite'
    inputs:
      mavenPomFile: 'pom.xml'
      goals: 'clean test'
      options: '-Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=$(SUITE_FILE) -Dbrowser=chrome -Dheadless=true -Denv=qa'

  - task: PublishTestResults@2
    displayName: 'Publish JUnit Results'
    condition: always()
    inputs:
      testResultsFormat: 'JUnit'
      testResultsFiles: '**/TEST-*.xml'
      mergeTestResults: true
      failTaskOnFailedTests: true
      testRunTitle: 'Automation - $(Build.BuildNumber)'

  - task: PublishPipelineArtifact@1
    displayName: 'Upload Extent Reports'
    condition: always()
    inputs:
      targetPath: 'target/extent-reports'
      artifact: 'test-reports'
      publishLocation: 'pipeline'

Automation Usage Patterns

  • PR validation: Use pr: trigger to run smoke suite on every pull request before merge.
  • Scheduled regression: Add schedules cron for nightly full regression against staging.
  • Multi-environment: Use pipeline parameters or variable groups for QA, staging, prod smoke.
  • Parallel browsers: Use strategy.matrix with browser dimension (similar to GitHub Actions).

Azure DevOps Test Plans Integration

Link automated test results to Test Plans test cases using the PublishTestResults@2 task with testRunTitle and associating test case IDs in your framework (e.g., TestNG @Test(testName = "TC-12345")). Test Plans shows pass/fail history per test case, requirement traceability, and manual vs automated coverage gaps.

# Associate results with Test Plans (requires test case IDs in result files)
- task: PublishTestResults@2
  inputs:
    testResultsFormat: 'JUnit'
    testResultsFiles: '**/TEST-*.xml'
    testPlan: '12345'
    testSuite: '67890'
    testRunTitle: 'Sprint 42 Regression'

GitHub Actions

What It Is

GitHub Actions is CI/CD built directly into GitHub. Workflows live in .github/workflows/ as YAML files. For automation engineers, it is ideal when code and CI live in the same place — no separate server, native PR checks, and a massive marketplace of reusable actions.

Workflow YAML for Automation

name: Automation Tests

on:
  push:
    branches: [main, develop]
  pull_request:
    branches: [main]
  workflow_dispatch:
    inputs:
      suite:
        description: 'TestNG suite file'
        required: true
        default: 'smoke.xml'
      environment:
        description: 'Target environment'
        required: true
        default: 'qa'

jobs:
  test:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    timeout-minutes: 60

    steps:
      - name: Checkout code
        uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Set up Java 17
        uses: actions/setup-java@v4
        with:
          java-version: '17'
          distribution: 'temurin'
          cache: 'maven'

      - name: Run automation suite
        run: >
          mvn clean test
          -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=${{ github.event.inputs.suite || 'smoke.xml' }}
          -Denv=${{ github.event.inputs.environment || 'qa' }}
          -Dbrowser=chrome
          -Dheadless=true

      - name: Publish test results
        uses: dorny/test-reporter@v1
        if: always()
        with:
          name: TestNG Results
          path: 'target/surefire-reports/*.xml'
          reporter: java-junit

      - name: Upload test reports
        uses: actions/upload-artifact@v4
        if: always()
        with:
          name: test-reports-${{ github.run_number }}
          path: |
            target/surefire-reports/
            target/extent-reports/
          retention-days: 14

Matrix Strategy for Cross-Browser Testing

jobs:
  cross-browser:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    strategy:
      fail-fast: false
      matrix:
        browser: [chrome, firefox]
        suite: [smoke.xml]

    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - uses: actions/setup-java@v4
        with:
          java-version: '17'
          distribution: 'temurin'
      - name: Run tests on ${{ matrix.browser }}
        run: >
          mvn clean test
          -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=${{ matrix.suite }}
          -Dbrowser=${{ matrix.browser }}
          -Dheadless=true
      - uses: actions/upload-artifact@v4
        if: always()
        with:
          name: reports-${{ matrix.browser }}
          path: target/surefire-reports/
Tip: Use fail-fast: false in matrix so one browser failure does not cancel others. Upload artifacts per matrix job for isolated debugging.

GitLab CI/CD

.gitlab-ci.yml Structure

GitLab CI uses a single .gitlab-ci.yml at the repo root. Pipelines are organized into stages; each job belongs to a stage and runs on GitLab Runners (shared or self-hosted).

stages:
  - build
  - test
  - report

variables:
  MAVEN_OPTS: "-Xmx1024m"
  SUITE: "smoke.xml"

build:
  stage: build
  image: maven:3.9-eclipse-temurin-17
  script:
    - mvn clean compile -DskipTests
  artifacts:
    paths:
      - target/classes/
    expire_in: 1 hour

smoke-test:
  stage: test
  image: maven:3.9-eclipse-temurin-17
  services:
